He Jingwu's Proposal for Air Force Organization Plan 73

Scattered Donations of Aircraft Cannot Save the Nation

The People Should Autonomously Establish an Air Force

Solicit Five Hundred Donation Units

Limit the Fundraising to Fifty Million Yuan by the End of This Year

Hankou Correspondence: He Jingwu, Commissioner of the Pinghan Railway, spoke at the railway's anniversary celebration the other day about the necessity of organizing a national air force. The following is a record of his speech: Colleagues, we bear two immense responsibilities. One is how to manage the Pinghan Railway well, and the other is how to save the nation. I have spoken a lot about the railway in the past. Today, let's discuss a major national issue, which is saving the nation through aviation. Why is aviation so important for saving the nation? Let me explain this in several points:

First, the necessity of air force equipment. The modern world is a world of air force competition. Since the September 18th Incident, the national crisis has worsened day by day. Many Chinese people have proposed ways to save the nation, and their theories are all correct, but unfortunately, no one has put them into practice. I, Jingwu, am a soldier and advocate resolute resistance. However, resistance requires military strength. What is our military strength like? China's navy has only 70,000 to 80,000 tons of warships. Japan's navy has more than ten times that tonnage. Can we compete with such a disparity? I don't think anyone in the navy would give a positive answer. What about the army? The Chinese army's ability to endure war is not weaker than Japan's. The Battle of Shanghai proved this. Although our weapons are slightly weaker, our spirit is excellent. Moreover, our land is vast. Their tanks and flat-trajectory guns, though powerful, can only be used on plains. We can leave the plains and engage them in close combat in the mountains. As in Jehol now, the enemy cannot use these powerful weapons. Each Japanese division has 12,000 men in peacetime and 25,000 men in wartime. Even if they send twenty divisions, that's only 500,000 men, which is not enough to divide forces across China. Nor can they shamelessly claim, as the Japanese militarists do, that they can occupy Shanghai in three hours and all of China in two weeks. As long as we wage a protracted war against them, victory will not necessarily belong to Japan. The number of our current army is probably dozens of times more than Japan's in the Northeast. Therefore, the army can fight. Our biggest difficulty is the air force. Japan's air force strength is about 2,000 aircraft. After deducting some for national defense, they can hypothetically fly about 1,000 aircraft to China. Warships, tanks, and flat-trajectory guns all have geographical limitations. Only aircraft can fly everywhere. If we don't have an air force to counter them and protect our airspace, they can use their superior aircraft to sweep across our important cities, bomb our arsenals, destroy our ordnance factories, and disrupt our transportation lines in the shortest time, making it impossible for our army to transport supplies, and our bullets cannot be replenished. We would lose our inherent fighting power. That's when we would truly suffer. This is why the Chinese people are frantically calling for saving the nation through aviation. I personally believe that although Chinese aircraft cannot fly to Japan to bomb them, we can make every effort to resist the incoming Japanese aircraft. For example, if Japan sends 1,000 aircraft, we can resist them if we have 500. In the Battle of Shanghai, the Japanese army failed repeatedly, and the navy did not inflict much damage on us. Our losses were entirely due to our inability to defend our airspace, and we were freely bombed by Japanese aircraft. If we had an air force comparable to Japan's to counter them, the Japanese aircraft could be driven away, and Zhabei would not have suffered such losses, and the army would have been victorious. Therefore, to strengthen our national defense, the only way is to increase our air force strength. Otherwise, we will never be able to maintain our national lifeline. Although we have a large population of 400 million and a good spirit, we can only perish together under the enemy's aircraft. The national crisis is imminent. We cannot expand our navy in the shortest time due to economic and time constraints. Only buying more aircraft is something that the people's wealth can achieve.

Second, the shortcomings of the air force in the past. China is not without an air force now, but why can't it fight against others? This is certainly due to the lack of numbers, but the biggest reason is the lack of an organized system. The country's aircraft have become the personal bodyguards of military men. Only individuals can use them, and the government has no power to control and dispatch them. Aviation personnel have also become soldiers of various departments, not soldiers of the country. We hear the sinking of the Flying Eagle warship and the explosion of aircraft in Sichuan. We can only wait for the country to perish. The equipment of the existing airfields in the country is also very rudimentary. Other manufacturing plants, ammunition factories, and material factories have not been prepared. If this situation is not improved, we cannot talk about defending the country, and we cannot talk about saving the country.

Third, the failures of donating aircraft in the past. Since the Battle of Shanghai, the Chinese people have deeply felt the importance of the air force. The call to save the nation through aviation has resounded throughout the country. Many patriotic people have voluntarily donated aircraft to the government. This is certainly very good, but these scattered donations, which are gradually destroyed, cannot increase the strength of national defense. The shortcoming is still the lack of an overall organization and system. Air force combat is not like the army, where a small force can defeat a larger force. It is entirely a matter of numerical proportion. Because the weapons on aircraft are limited, the combat power of each aircraft cannot be very different. A small number of aircraft will naturally be destroyed by a large number of aircraft. Last year, during the Battle of Shanghai, twelve Japanese aircraft attacked Hangzhou, and we countered with six aircraft. Although we destroyed two of them, we ultimately failed. Also, in the Suzhou area, one of our fighter aircraft, piloted by an American, was surrounded by four Japanese aircraft and was shot down. The pilot also died in the line of duty. Therefore, air force combat must concentrate forces to win.

Fourth, how should we organize the air force? The importance of the air force and the shortcomings of our country's air force in the past have been described above. How should we remedy and reverse this in the future? I believe that the only way is for the people to organize themselves automatically. I now formally propose that the Pinghan Railway initiate the establishment of a National Air Force Founding Association to publicize it nationwide and create five hundred units, each unit donating one aircraft. We, the Pinghan Railway, will establish the National Air Force Founding Association starting today. All employees of the railway are members of the branch association and will first pledge to donate one aircraft, named "Pinghan." Then, we will persuade various roads, provinces, cities, counties, legal entities, and patriotic people across the country to donate. If each major road donates one aircraft and several smaller roads jointly donate one aircraft, we can obtain ten units from the railway industry alone. In addition, we can obtain at least five or six aircraft from the postal and telegraph services. The Seamen's Union is powerful and can also pledge to donate several aircraft. In total, the transportation industry can pledge twenty units. China has more than 1,000 counties. If each large county donates one aircraft and two or three small counties jointly donate one aircraft, we can obtain hundreds of units. In addition, if various provinces, special cities, agencies, professional groups, and public-spirited capitalists, all aware that the country will soon perish, generously donate, I think it will not be difficult to raise 500 units. These 500 units should be completed by the end of 1933. At the same time, the National Air Force Founding Association should be established in Shanghai. We should then petition the government to expand the existing Aviation Administration into the Air Force Department and, together with the National Air Force Founding Association, establish the procedures for air force construction, actively prepare aircraft material factories, ammunition factories, and airfields, and train at least 500 pilots each year. In this way, the Chinese air force will be planned, organized, whole rather than scattered, national rather than privately owned, and used for national defense rather than for internal warfare. With this great force to defend against enemy aircraft attacks and protect our army, we can certainly achieve great results in military affairs. This is my proposal. The rise and fall of the world are the responsibility of every individual. If my patriotic colleagues think this is feasible, let's organize ourselves. Let's designate this week as the day for external publicity. All employees should be divided into groups to promote the significance of saving the nation through aviation. Everything depends on human effort. As long as we work hard, there is nothing we cannot achieve. This issue concerns the lifeblood of the country and is the responsibility of every individual. To save the nation, each individual must do it themselves. We must not passively hope that others will do it while forgetting ourselves, nor should we underestimate ourselves and think that we are insignificant. Men of the Pinghan Railway, come, let's combine our hot blood with the hot blood of our compatriots across the country, organize a national air force to save the nation, and fight to the death with the powerful enemy.

The Shandong Militia Corps Will Restore Its Old Strength

Augmenting the Military Force of the People 74

Jinan Correspondence: In recent years, Shandong Province has been actively reorganizing the militia corps and has achieved considerable results. Recently, the provincial government, deeply concerned about the daily increasing foreign aggression, has changed the four militia districts into five routes and intensified training. Li Shuchun, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, also submitted a memorandum to the provincial government last month regarding the reform of the militia corps, advocating the restoration of the old militia corps strength: 300 for first-class counties, 200 for second-class counties, and 100 for third-class counties, and the purchase of additional firearms and the organization of bare-handed broadsword teams to augment the military force of the people. In addition, he also made recommendations on the establishment of special management agencies and the distribution of militia corps salaries. The memorandum was sent to the Departments of Civil Affairs and Finance for review. According to the reply, it was deemed inappropriate to make changes mid-year as the twenty-first year had not yet ended. It was suggested to reconsider the local conditions in the twenty-second year and submit a request for approval. At today's (3rd) provincial government administrative meeting, the case was brought up for discussion again. It was resolved to approve the proposal. The original text of the proposal is recorded on the left: "Report from the Secretariat: The Departments of Civil Affairs and Finance jointly reported that they were ordered to review the memorandum submitted by the Department of Civil Affairs regarding the organization and training of the militia corps. After careful review, it was found that all the items listed in the memorandum under the headings 1) System, 2) Training, and 3) Organization were appropriate and should be approved as proposed. However, there are three items that should be specially regulated, which have also been agreed upon after consultation, and the measures are presented below: 1) Regarding the establishment of a special management agency for the proposed militia corps headquarters, it is proposed that the government set up a militia corps section in the responsible department or designate several officials to handle militia corps affairs exclusively. 2) Regarding the militia corps salaries proposed in the original memorandum for each county, which should be submitted by each county to the Department of Finance for transfer to the district command headquarters for monthly distribution, this method of transferring and disbursing is too cumbersome and difficult. It should continue to be handled according to the current method, with the county government issuing the salaries nearby each month and reporting to the headquarters and district headquarters for record-keeping. 3) Regarding the restoration of the old militia corps strength in each county (i.e., 300 for first-class counties, 200 for second-class counties, and 100 for third-class counties) and the purchase of additional firearms and the organization of bare-handed broadsword teams, the current number of militia corps and salaries in each county have already been approved by the government and included in the twenty-first year's county local budget. It is not appropriate to make changes mid-year. It should continue to be handled according to the current year's budget. It is suggested to reconsider the local conditions in the twenty-second year and submit a request for approval. The above three items have been repeatedly discussed, and the opinions are the same. Is this appropriate? Please submit for approval. If approved, please issue an order for implementation, etc."

The Daladier Cabinet is Increasingly Unstable

The Socialist Party Will Not Join the Government, and the Central Parties Will Not Support It 75

Paris, 6th (National Telegram): The position of the French Daladier Cabinet is now increasingly unstable, as the executive committee of the Socialist Party decided today not to join the new government. Their support for the government is entirely dependent on whether the government can vigorously implement radical policies. If the government cannot implement radical policies, the Socialist Party members in the parliament will vote against the government. The current public opinion circles believe that the Daladier Cabinet, under such circumstances, will fail if it cannot obtain the support of the central parties. However, the central parties may not necessarily have any goodwill towards the new government either.

Paris, 5th (Havas): At a public banquet held by the Republican press, President Lebrun stated that the current situation is serious and that immediate efforts are needed to improve the financial situation. However, the expressions of various regions seem to resist this effort. Therefore, the task of the press at present is to eliminate temporary impulses, rectify the situation, and advise the people to assist the country within their proper scope.

Paris, 5th (Havas): The Socialist Party's national executive committee continued its meeting in the evening. Representative Lelorre supported joining the cabinet, saying that this was necessary to maintain the left-wing majority. Then, the party leader Blum explained in detail the activities of the party's representatives, saying that the party should not be bound by the two issues of supporting or opposing joining the cabinet, because even if it does not join the cabinet, there are still those who can be assisted. Blum said that he hoped the Daladier cabinet could last for a long time. He believed that there was a danger of the parliamentary majority party changing direction. If the Socialist Party did not firmly oppose the government, this danger could be avoided. In his view, there was a great possibility for the Socialist and Radical parties to reconcile with each other to maintain the cabinet. However, several party members proposed motions that contradicted his opinions. Despite Blum's best efforts to persuade them, they were not withdrawn. One motion advocated adhering to the decision of the party's national congress and leaving the issue of joining the cabinet to the party's national congress for further decision. The request from the Radical Party to form a standing committee jointly by the two parties was rejected. This motion was passed with 2,636 votes.

Marseille, 5th (Havas): Members of the central and right-wing Republican parties held an important meeting, chaired by Representative, former cabinet member, and Vice-President of the Republican Federation, Lybert. Lybert emphasized that the situation was serious, and the majority party showed incompetence after the general election of the parliament. Therefore, the various parties should be reorganized and a cabinet with a definite backing should be formed in order to implement necessary reforms.

Mutiny in the Dutch Navy 76

Officers Imprisoned, Ships Seized, and Escape

The Hague Authorities Dispatched Ships to Pursue and Arrest

The Hague, 5th (National News Agency): After the Dutch Navy reduced salaries, soldiers stationed in Asia harbored resentment. There had already been two instances of insubordination within a week. Recently, there was a mutiny and ship seizure, becoming the most serious situation in the history of the Dutch Navy stationed in Asia. This time, the ships were returning to Oelee Harbour after exercises in the Celebes Sea. All the senior officers went ashore, and soldiers on the cruiser HNLMS Tromp suddenly imprisoned nine junior officers and seized the ship. It is now being pursued by the auxiliary ship HNLMS Altair and several gunboats. Naval personnel here, based on reports from the Governor of Northwest Sumatra, are deeply concerned that the mutinous soldiers will suddenly enter Surabaya, occupy the port, and release the four hundred insubordinate sailors who were arrested a few days ago. This is because the Governor received a report from a gunboat stating that the cruiser was seen west of Meulaboh in Northwest Sumatra Province, heading towards Surabaya at full speed. The pursuing ships are clearly communicating with the mutinous ship by radio, so they reported to the Governor that the mutineers seized the ammunition depot before imprisoning the officers, so they have ample ammunition and are prepared to resist. However, it is still unknown whether the Dutch fleet is prepared to besiege the ship at sea or force it to enter Surabaya Harbour.

Flying Fever in England 77

London, 6th (Reuters): The famous aviator Jim Mollison took off from Lympne Airport at 8:11 this morning in his aircraft, "The Heart's Content," bound for Natal, Brazil, with an estimated flight time of three and a half days. About an hour before Mollison's departure, Squadron Leader Gayford and Flight Lieutenant Nicholetts also took off from Cranwell in their aircraft bound for Cape Town, planning to fly non-stop. If all goes well, they will reach Tunis tomorrow. This trip requires flying 5,074 miles to break the long-distance record set by the Americans Boardman and Polando from New York to Constantinople. The aircraft is equipped with an automatic pilot, whose accuracy cannot be matched even by the most skilled pilots.

Cranwell, 6th (National News Agency): Royal Air Force Squadron Leader Gayford and Flight Lieutenant Nicholetts took off from here at 7:15 this morning in a specially made Fairey Long-Range Monoplane, intending to fly non-stop directly to Plettenberg Bay, aiming to break the world long-distance aviation record held by the United States. The world record was set by American aviators Boardman and Polando in July 1931, flying non-stop from New York to Istanbul, a distance of 5,012 miles. Today's flight from Cranwell to Cape Town is about 6,000 miles, and it is planned to fly for sixty hours.

After the Communist Bandits Fled into Sichuan Province 78

The Bandits are Fleeing in Two Routes

They are Now Being Heavily Besieged by Various Armies

Chengdu Correspondence: The Communist bandits He Long, Kuang Jixun, and Xu Xiangqian, unable to establish a foothold in the coal mines on the border of Shaanxi, took advantage of the chaotic situation in Sichuan to attack Sichuan. One part attacked Sichuan from the north of Shaanxi, while another part was active in Chengkou and Badong, attacking the main force in northern Sichuan, namely Xu Xiangqian, and the forces active in Chengkou and Badong were He Long and Kuang Jixun. The purpose of these two forces combined was to seize the entire northern Sichuan. At that time, the Sichuan warlords underestimated the strength of the bandits. Only after the fall of counties such as Chengkou and Tongjiang did they become alarmed and urgently mobilized troops to block them.

Before Kuang Jixun's troops entered Sichuan, villages near the Wanyuan and Zhuxi passes were suddenly looted by bandits, killing many local security personnel and posting reactionary slogans, which were naturally the work of the Communist bandits. Liu Cunhou, the Sichuan-Shaanxi Border Defense Commissioner stationed in Suiding, ordered Commander Liao Liangchen stationed in Dongxiang, Chengkou, and Wanyuan to guard the key passes of Lianghekou and Zhuyemiao, while also transferring his younger brother Liu Zhaogan's division from Chengdu to return to Suiding to defend. As a result, the reinforcements did not arrive, and Chengkou had already fallen, greatly alarming Wanyuan and Suiding. At the same time, Liu Zhaogan's division had won considerable victories in participating in the Allied Forces' operations and was confronting the 24th Army between Chengdu and Shuangliu. He was unwilling to be transferred back to Suiding to suppress the bandits and was preparing to seek new opportunities in the future. Under this extremely anxious situation, Liu Cunhou appealed to the various Sichuan armies to cease fighting and suppress the bandits together, while also contacting the Shaanxi authorities for joint suppression. At this time, the Central Army's two divisions under Hu Zongnan and Liu Maoen were pursuing the Communist bandits. Chengkou was recovered by Liu's division, and Kuang Jixun and his troops changed their strategy and dispersed. One group went deep into the interior of Sichuan towards Wanyuan and Suiding, while another group developed towards Tongjiang, Zhaohua, and Guangyuan. Because Kuang Jixun was originally a Sichuan soldier, he was very familiar with the terrain of Sichuan Province and the internal situation of the Sichuan army.

Tongjiang and Nanjiang bordered Shaanxi Province. After years of exploitation by troops and local bullies, the local vitality had long been exhausted. In addition, there had been continuous droughts and a vast disaster area. Since the outbreak of the Sichuan War, after Tian Songyao became the main force of the Sichuan War, the remote areas were particularly heavily taxed for military expenses, and the people could not afford to supply them. This environment was conducive to the incitement of communism. Tongjiang and Nanjiang had previously been dens of bandits. Now that the Communist Party had infiltrated, the previously hidden bandits were revived. Before Kuang Jixun and his troops reached Tongjiang and Nanjiang, peasants in Tongjiang suddenly rioted, stormed into the city, destroyed the county government, and the county magistrate was killed. A mutiny also occurred in Nanjiang at the same time, responding to the Communist bandits. More local farmers, unable to pay the exorbitant taxes, also became peasant bandits. They occupied the mountains, with bandits with guns in the inner layer and bandits with bare hands in the outer layer. As a result, Kuang Jixun and his troops gained great momentum and spread to Bazhong, Cangxi, and other places in southern Sichuan. Kuang intended that once Bazhong was captured, he could drive straight into the entire northern Sichuan, and then attack Yingshan and Qu County from the Jiangkou Township of Bazhong. Moreover, before Kuang's troops reached Bazhong and other places, Zhang Youqi and others in Sunjia Temple in Nanbu County dragged away the local militia, raised the red flag, and planned to lead their troops to attack Nanbu County. It was also reported that Gong Xinyi and Liu Kunlun, bandits in Shunqing and Pengxi, were also in contact with Kuang's troops. At that time, the city of Nanbu was closed, and there was great panic. When the 25th Regiment of the Third Division of Tian Songyao's 29th Army stationed in Nanchong heard the news and rushed to the scene, Zhang Youqi led his troops and thousands of farmers to the Siyi Market, Jinxiangu, and Dongjiao Temple areas near Cangxi in the south. Government troops are now tracking and pursuing them.

It is reported that the participants in the bandit suppression in Tian's army include the First Route under Li Weiruo, the Second Route under Liu Hanxiong, the 14th Brigade under Luo Shaolin, the Garrison Commander Tian Zefu, one brigade of the Third Division under Luo Naiqiong, and the entire Independent Division under Fen Jiantang, totaling more than twenty regiments. The two divisions of the Central Army under Hu Zongnan and Liu Maoen, and the Shaanxi Army under Wang Zhiyuan, who entered Sichuan from southern Shaanxi, have established contact with Liu Cunhou's troops and are implementing a strategy of encircling the Communist bandits. Therefore, the Communist bandits will not easily succeed.

New Book Donation to Shandong Library 80

Leftover from Henan's Liu Chunzhai

Ninety Boxes of Books, Calligraphy and Paintings

Jinan Correspondence: Liu Chunzhai from Zhigou, Henan, was a renowned book collector. He once traveled to Shandong for business. When he passed away the year before last, he left a will donating sixty-eight boxes of books to the Shandong Library. The library had already requested the provincial government to send personnel to oversee the inventory. Besides these sixty-eight boxes, there were also twenty-two boxes of calligraphy and paintings. Because Liu owed debts to Xu Xiaohang and Wei Fucun, the court ordered an auction to repay the debts. After negotiations by the library, the twenty-two boxes of calligraphy and paintings were donated to the library under the names of Xu and Wei. The library provided 750 yuan to prevent losses and gave Liu's family 1,000 yuan as funeral expenses for Liu Chunzhai. The Department of Education submitted this matter to the provincial government's political affairs meeting on the 3rd, and it was resolved to approve the proposal. The original text of the Education Department's proposal is recorded below: "According to the report from Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, Mr. Liu from Fugou, Henan, donated sixty-eight boxes of books to our library, which were previously inventoried by personnel sent by the provincial government. In addition, there are twenty-two boxes of calligraphy and books. Because Liu owed debts to Xu Xiaohang and Wei Fucun, the Jinan District Court auctioned them off at the request of the creditors to repay the debts. Our library believes that these books were clearly designated for the library in the will of Liu's ancestor, Mr. Chunzhai, so their ownership no longer belongs to his descendants and cannot be used to repay debts. At the same time, Liu's descendants are donating these books to our library, and our library has the right to accept them according to law. We have already submitted a request to your department to send a letter to the High Court to demand their return. Our library has also filed an objection with the Jinan District Court. After several court sessions, the creditors are willing to give up the right to auction and return the items to our library. Moreover, Liu had already gone bankrupt and had no other property to repay the debts. The value of the books is used as Liu's debt repayment. Although the procedure for donating the books to our library under the names of Xu and Wei has changed, the original intention has been achieved. We should gladly accept it. After inspecting the calligraphy and paintings, the Jinan District Court initially estimated their value at 2,639.5 yuan. Xu and Wei are not wealthy. Although they are generously donating to the public, according to principles of fairness, the government should provide them with a small subsidy to show its consideration, intending to give them 750 yuan to avoid losses and to encourage donations from all sectors. Furthermore, Mr. Liu Shigu, a descendant of the ancient gentleman Liu, donated sixty-eight boxes of books according to the will of his grandfather, Mr. Chunzhai, estimated to be worth more than 20,000 yuan, which is the largest donation since the library's establishment. However, Liu suffered losses in business, and his property was sold off. Mr. Chunzhai's coffin is still in Jinan, and there is no money to transport it back to his hometown. The government should also provide some assistance to alleviate his suffering, intending to award 1,000 yuan for funeral expenses, to be received by his grandson, Shigu, to transport the coffin back to his hometown on a specified date for funeral purposes, so as to prevent creditors from seizing it. All two items of expenses, totaling 1,750 yuan, should be budgeted and submitted for approval and allocation." Based on this, Liu and Xu, Wei, donate significant book and calligraphy worth a great deal to the library. It is deemed appropriate to grant 1,000 yuan for Liu's funeral expenses and 750 yuan to subsidize Xu and Wei for the book value, respectively. It should be covered by the 21st year of education preparatory expenses item, should it be approved or not, please make a decision." (4th)

Bandits in Songjiang Resist Arrest, Killing Soldiers 81

On the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway tracks at the 31st Foreign Bridge in Shihudang, a village within the county, at around 6 PM on the 5th of this month, a cake vendor was selling his goods when three bandits suddenly came forward and robbed him of over 1,900 copper coins. He immediately reported to the nearby Third Battalion, Twelfth Company police outpost of the Second Security Regiment, which was stationed to guard the bridge. Guard soldier Wu Nairu went to pursue and caught one of the bandits, confiscating a homemade pistol, a small firearm, and eight bullets from his person. He brought the bandit back to the outpost for questioning. Around 11 PM, more than ten bandits suddenly arrived, carrying about five or six handguns. They stormed into the outpost, intending to rob and free the captured bandit. Seeing this, the guards ordered the group to disperse in preparation to capture the arriving bandits. The bandits opened fire, and the captured bandit took the opportunity to escape by swimming away. Soldier Wu bravely pursued them but was shot in the left chest by the bandits. The bullet did not pass through, and he died instantly. The remaining soldiers returned fire, and bullets flew everywhere. Another bandit was re-captured, suffering a gunshot wound to the forehead. The bandits, unable to withstand the force, scattered and fled. However, the area is crisscrossed by waterways and is a known haunt for bandits, and it was already late at night, so they were not pursued further. On the afternoon of the 6th, the captured bandit was escorted to the regimental headquarters. After a preliminary interrogation by Deputy Regiment Commander Wan, he confessed his name as Li Runfa, 28 years old, from Ningbo. He had previously served as a soldier in the Third Company of the First Security Battalion of Zhejiang and had committed robberies in Jiaxing, Pinghu, and other places. He did not deny the robbery of the cake vendor's copper coins and resisting arrest. During the incident, in addition to guard soldier Wu Nairu's immediate death, two small firearms were damaged by the bandits. The bandit is currently temporarily detained in the county prison, and the soldier's body has been transported to Songjiang, awaiting family members to arrive to collect it for burial.

Pirates Attack Litchuan Steamboat in Suzhou 82

The Litchuan and River China (Hehua) small steamships of the Suzhou China Merchants Inland River Steamship Bureau usually carry passengers between Suzhou and Hangzhou. On the 5th, the Litchuan ship towed a scrap ship from the Waste Profits Company and a pig boat, carrying more than 50 passengers. It departed from Suzhou at 3 PM. Two plainclothes bandits were mixed among the passengers. When the ship passed Wujiang, five more bandits disguised as passengers and disembarked. When the ship reached Duiqiao, the seven bandits pulled out handguns, threatened to stop the ship, and robbed at will. A hotel worker was robbed of 150 yuan, a butcher lost 50 yuan, and a female passenger lost a gold bracelet. In total, approximately 500 to 600 yuan in cash was robbed. The bandits then jumped into the pig boat, untied the rope, and fled.

Establishment of the Wuxian County Defense Corps 83

The township defense corps in various districts of Wuxian County have been established, with over 4,000 members. However, uniforms and firearms require approximately hundreds of thousands of yuan. In addition to establishing a firearms purchasing committee to engage in fundraising, the County Defense Committee plans to hold a meeting soon to actively conduct large-scale planning.

Six Financial Houses Close 84

Business in Suzhou is sluggish. By the end of last year, a total of six financial houses, one gold shop, and one silk brocade shop had closed, laying off seven or eight hundred employees and associates. Most other shops are also engaged in downsizing.

Expansion Project Begins on Xiyang Road in Wuxi 85

After the January 28th Shanghai Incident last year, the county government and the Construction Bureau received orders to build a road from Wuxi to Changshu. To facilitate traffic, the original road was widened to five feet, up to Yangjian Town at the border of Wuxi. Now, Construction Bureau Chief Xiao Zicai believes that the road needs to be further widened. Therefore, he is using the unified rickshaw tax revenue to widen the entire road by five feet, making it ten feet wide. Construction began yesterday and will soon be completed.

Punishment for Murderers in Pingchao Bloodshed in Nantong 86

The Nantong Pingchao District Defense Corps forcibly collected donations, resulting in the brutal murder of eight villagers in a bloody incident. After investigation by Provincial Committee Member Wu Xizheng, the main culprits in this case, Wang ZhengGang, Kang ZhiChao, Chen ShuFang, and others, have been removed from their administrative positions. Because the case involves human lives, it should be handled judicially. Therefore, the county civil association and others sent a telegram to the provincial government requesting instructions, and the culprits were transferred to the court.

Hangzhou Aviation School Plane Crash During Exercise 87

Zhang Yuheng, the squadron leader of the second squadron of the Jianqiao Central Aviation School's flight team, crashed while practicing flying in (missing name). Because the area had towering trees, when landing at the airfield, the wind was strong and the plane was heavy. About a hundred feet above the ground, it hit a tree and nosedived. The plane was slightly damaged, and Zhang suffered minor abrasions on his face, lips, and chest. His knees were more seriously injured. He was sent to Guangji Hospital for treatment. Except for his left knee, which still needs to be examined by X-ray for any fractures, the other injuries are not serious. Zhang is from Hefei, Anhui. He graduated from Jinan Aviation School in 1925. He has participated in various campaigns to suppress rebellion and bandits. He came to Hangzhou last September to assume his current position.

Local News

Chen Youren Expresses His Diplomatic Views on Japan 88

States That His Advocacy for Severing Relations Has Not Changed

Will Definitely Not Lead to a World War

Former Foreign Minister Chen Youren, after returning to Shanghai from Europe the night before last, has sparked much speculation about his sudden return home. Yesterday at 6 PM, Chen met with reporters from Chinese and Western newspapers at his residence on Avenue Road. Chen stated that he would not be going to Nanjing for the time being, nor would he be willing to take on any position. As for his advocacy for severing relations with Japan, it has not changed. The summary of his conversation is as follows:

Tired of Traveling, Now Returning Home 89

Reporters first asked Chen if he had any mission upon returning to Shanghai and whether he was responding to a government summons. Chen said that he was living in exile. He went abroad to Europe for travel in June last year and has been away for seven months. Therefore, he is returning home because he is tired of traveling. He was not summoned by anyone in the government, nor does he have any mission.

Advocacy Unchanged 90

Chen continued to answer reporters' questions, stating that his previous advocacy for severing relations with Japan and other opinions remains unchanged. Regarding the international situation, he said that other countries view us as beggars pleading for sympathy. He also believes that our country should mobilize the entire nation as one to show that we are not weak and do not rely solely on others. Only in this way can we gain international respect. Otherwise, as it is today, we are completely relying on the League of Nations, giving other countries the impression that we are underestimating our country's position. No one pays attention to the mournful sound of a beggar. Moreover, Japan has already exchanged views with Britain and France on the League of Nations. To Britain, they mentioned Britain's India in the Far East. To France, they mentioned French Annam. Therefore, Britain and France, each for their own interests, are unwilling to become enemies with Japan. Our pleas to others will only end up as an illusion.

Will Not Cause a Major War 91

Chen also stated that even if the Manchurian problem leads to a split, it will definitely not lead to a second world war, because the United States would definitely not dare to declare war today, unless Britain and the United States unite and confront Japan together. However, there is no possibility of cooperation between Britain and the United States. Chen did not give his reasons for why Britain and the United States cannot unite, but it is rumored that there are complex war debt issues between Britain and the United States.

What is the Diplomatic Strategy? 92

Chen also said that all countries have their own set diplomatic policies. Therefore, when handling diplomacy, they only need to proceed according to their established diplomatic policies. For example, when British Ambassador Lampson is stationed in China, all matters can be freely conducted according to his country's long-standing policies, with a complete framework for handling them. What is our country's diplomatic policy?

Moral Sanctions 93

When Chen spoke about foreign affairs, he cited Japanese history from 1867 as proof. He continued to say that relying on the League of Nations will ultimately fail. The League of Nations can only impose moral sanctions. Relying solely on the League of Nations is useless. He believes that we should have already issued a declaration to the Kellogg-Briand Pact and the countries in the Washington Conference (i.e., the Nine-Power Treaty), urging them to convene a meeting. The main purpose is to have the United States formally participate, so that the resolution has the power to be implemented in reality. Regarding the issue of the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, Chen believes that this is only the restoration of diplomatic relations. There should be further work. In addition, Chen also mentioned the issue of economic boycott of Japanese goods, saying that the current economic severance of relations is not enough to cause any loss to Japanese businesses, because Japanese goods can still be imported into China in disguise through India. Finally, Chen said that he would not go to Nanjing, because even if he were to become the Foreign Minister, he would still not be able to exert his authority to realize his advocacy. Therefore, what is the point of going to Nanjing?

Finance Minister Song's Cold Has Recovered 94

Acting Premier Song Ziwen's cold has gradually recovered after days of medical treatment. Yesterday at 3 PM, Song invited local association members Shi Liangcai, Yang Zhixiong, Huang Renzhi, and others to a tea party at his residence and discussed everything until about 5 PM when they dispersed.

Duan Qirui recently came to Shanghai from Tianjin with his nephew Duan Honggang and Wu Guangxin, and is still staying at the World College on Route Ferguson. He has not yet moved to his new house on Avenue Joffre. In recent days, various circles and old friends have been hosting banquets for Duan Qirui every night. Aviation Expert Mr. Wang Bide from Hangxian Returns Home 96

Yesterday, Mr. Wang Bide from Hangxian returned to China on the Italian mail ship "Gauze." Mr. Wang is a graduate of the St. John's Youth School. In 1921, he went to the Bleriot Aviation School in France to study aviation technology. After being examined by the International Aeronautics Federation, he received a diploma. Twenty years later, he went to the Bleriot Aviation School in France again to study aviation technology. In 1922, he also studied aerial tactics at the Littorio Military Aviation School in Rome and obtained a diploma. Mr. Wang is only thirty years old and is full of energy. At a time when our country is actively promoting aviation, it is believed that Mr. Wang will be able to use what he has learned to serve the country. It is said that Mr. Wang encountered danger five times during his studies, but he was able to turn danger into safety, which shows his excellent skills.

The All-Shanghai Real Estate Industry Holds an Emergency Meeting Yesterday Regarding the Water Fee Dispute 102

Resolved to Issue a Declaration Jointly with the Western Property Owners Association

The Public Works Department Held a Meeting to Discuss the Case Yesterday

Representatives of Chinese and Western Property Owners Met with the Secretary of the Public Works Department Yesterday

The Shanghai Real Estate Association, in view of the fact that the British-owned Water Company has installed water meters and increased water charges by several times compared to before, causing not only extra losses to landlords but also unsettling to the city's residents, convened an emergency meeting at the association yesterday afternoon at 4 PM to discuss response measures. In the morning, Dou Yaoting, a member of the association's standing committee, along with the two chairmen of the Western Property Owners Association, met with Jones, the Secretary of the Public Works Department, to report that the current water fee problem has reached a serious stage. The details are as follows:

Members Present 103

Around 3 PM in the afternoon, representatives from various property owners arrived at the meeting, including representatives from Delly, Yicheng, Xiyuan, Gu Lanji, Central Trust Company, Dong Yu, Cheng Yu, Changtai, Taili, Xinghe, Yizhong Yin Company, Yongqing Ruiji, Darley Accountants, Zhongde, Xichangxing, Zhonghe, China Land Reclamation Bank, Gaochang, Xu Xiangji, the trust department of the Continental Bank, Zhenyi, Mingchang, Wei Chengji, He Kun Trust Company, Jingji, Yide, Yunji, Fenxing, Hexing, Jiuxing, Shenyutang, Donglai Bank, Zhou Gengji, Changfeng, Dayufeng, Xiangmao Foreign Firm, Longzhang, Huada, Sanjin, Zhenye, Xielong, Jingqin, and China Business Company. The representatives included Chen Bingqian, Shen Jixuan, Yan Zhusan, Jiang Bingsheng, Wang Zihou, Pang Xiangchen, Dou Yaoting, Li Bohan, and Guo Zusheng, totaling over two hundred people.

Important Matters Resolved 104

Chairman Shen Jixuan and recorders Tao Leqin and Zeng Xianyuan started by having Standing Committee Member Li Bohan report on the disputes after the installation of water meters. Then, representatives from Delly Company, Qinyu Company, Yizhong Yin Company, Darley Accountants, and others reported on the circumstances of their water being cut off by the Water Company. Next, Standing Committee Member Dou Yaoting reported on the circumstances of contacting the Water Company after the water was cut off in various places, and the meeting with the Secretary of the Public Works Department. After everyone expressed their opinions, they were very agitated about the Water Company's sudden water cutoff. The chairman summarized the opinions and resolved the following important matters: 1. Issue a joint declaration with the Western Property Owners Association. 2. The issue of universal water meter installation will be resolved after the results of the Public Works Committee meeting this afternoon (today). 3. If the Water Company continues to cut off the water or cuts it off without turning it back on, implement emergency self-defense measures permitted by law. 4. Schedule a reception for various sectors to explain the content of the water case and its relationship to the interests of various sectors. 5. Upon receiving the Western Property Owners Association's notification, inform each property owner to make a blank form report, submit it to the police station for record-keeping every month, and send a letter to the police station to prepare and issue blank forms. Other cases were then discussed and the meeting adjourned.

Water Cutoffs in Various Places 105

During yesterday's meeting, various representatives reported the following situations: 1. Delly Company's water to Huasheng Road, Fenzhou Road, and Bolu in Yangshupu was cut off at 11 AM on December 5th of last year. The tenants reopened it themselves. 2. The water to more than one hundred buildings of Huada Company on Zhoujiazui Road and Shuncheng Li in Yangshupu was cut off, with the monthly charge still being the same with the package delivery. The total stopcock was closed on December 15th, at 3 PM. The company still did not turn the water back on. For a hundred buildings in Yuanfu Li on Tangpu Road and Baoding Road, the water company used water meters from July. The water fees increased by more than four times. On January 24th, the company sent a letter to each tenant saying that if the water fee was not paid, they would have to stop supplying water. At 2 PM on the 2nd of this month, the water was cut off. The tenants reopened it themselves. 3. Fenxing Company received a letter from the water company stating that it owed more than 150 yuan and must be paid before February 1st, otherwise the water would be cut off. The company's water was cut off on the 2nd. The tenants jointly discussed and reopened it themselves. 4. The water to two hundred and fifty buildings of Yizhong Yin Company in Huaxin Fang on Yangshupu Road was cut off twice on February 2nd and 3rd. 5. Qinyu Company's water to houses numbered 5 to 137 in Qinyu Li on Linqing Road in Yangshupu, was a packaged-water arrangement, and the total cost for July to December was 436.65 yuan. On January 17th, an immediate bank check was sent, but the company returned it and refused to accept it. The water was cut off on February 3rd. The tenants reopened it themselves. The company then closed it again and sent people to guard it. The tenants still freely turned on the water. 6. The water to Jinyang Li on Beidier Road in Yangshupu, represented by China Business Company, was cut off by the water company at 9:30 AM on February 1st.

Negotiation Process 106

Yesterday morning, Dou Yaoting, a member of the standing committee of the Real Estate Association, along with Mr. and Mrs. Plosserden and Mr. Spike, the chairmen of the Western Property Owners Association, went to the Public Works Department and met with Secretary Jones. Dou and others explained that after the water company installed the main water meter, the water fees had skyrocketed. They pointed out that the water company's water price had already increased to 7.5%, so there was no need to worry about the company losing money. The company's revenue had greatly increased since the actual delivery. On the other hand, the landlords had suffered a great loss. The water cutoff issue had now reached a serious state in the city. As the highest administrative body in the concession, the Public Works Department should pay attention to it. The Secretary asked for the specific opinions of the property owners. Dou explained that the memorandum submitted to the Public Works Department the other day was the opinion of the property owners. At that time, the Secretary replied that the case had been submitted to the Public Works Committee for discussion this afternoon (6th), and that a reply would be given as soon as the results were available, stating that the installation of water meters by the Water Company was imperative, but that another method would be used in the future so that property owners would not suffer significant losses. After speaking, Dou and others left.

Mr. Feng's Opinion 107

Regarding the issue of universally installing water meters, Feng Bingnan has been actively mediating. Our reporter obtained Mr. Feng's suggestions in a written statement to the Public Works Department, which are translated as follows: ("Mr. Feng Bingnan's Opinion on the Issue of Universal Water Meter Installation" - Abridged Translation of Mr. Feng's Letter to the Public Works Department, December 5, 1932). Since the water meter contract was signed between the Public Works Department and the Shanghai Waterworks Company on December 24, 1931, the Waterworks Company has been installing water meters within the settlement. Since the trial use of metered water billing began, water bills have sharply increased, with some even quadrupling or ninefold the original cost. As it is customary in Shanghai for water fees to be included in the rent and collected by landlords on behalf of the company, the increased water fees primarily affect landlords. The Real Estate Association has risen in opposition, and negotiations have been protracted without resolution. Currently, landlords and the company find it difficult to reach an agreement. Prior to the twelfth year [of the Republic], officials of the Public Works Department foresaw this issue. The Chief Officer at the time drafted a memorandum stating, "Water meter prices should be graded so that after meter installation, the water price paid by users will not be higher than the packaged water system. As for Chinese-style houses, due to Shanghai's customs, fees are paid by landlords. Therefore, legal protection should be provided to prevent tenants from wasting water to protect the interests of landlords." His intention was, "The company should first select fifty households for trial meter installation to test the average water consumption and then determine the value of the water meter accordingly." Metered billing means the monthly fees fluctuate, with no fixed amount compared to the previous month. However, rent is fixed monthly and cannot increase or decrease with water prices. This is obvious. Furthermore, landlords cannot restrict tenants' water usage. Due to these two reasons, the Real Estate Association strongly opposes the Waterworks Company's plan to universally install water meters. The Chief of the Public Works Department of the Public Works Bureau stated at the Public Works Committee meeting on November 16, 1931, "Due to the current Shanghai custom, water fees are paid directly by landlords, not tenants. Therefore, it is difficult to predict whether installing water meters will achieve the goal of saving expenses." Therefore, unless users become direct payers, there will inevitably be a day when rental income is insufficient to cover water fees. Mr. Hill also only conditionally approved of universally installing water meters. Summarizing Mr. Hill's opinion, it stated that if Shanghai and American cities had identical customs and systems, universal water meter installation would be as effective in preventing waste as it is in American cities. However, if Shanghai has customs not found in America, the effectiveness of universal water meter installation compared to American cities becomes questionable. Regarding water meter prices, the contract between the Public Works Department and the Waterworks Company stipulates they are too high and not based on actual field testing. The Waterworks Company has discounts for users billed by meter, indicating the company also recognizes its prices are expensive. Mr. Hill believed water meter prices should not increase the burden on poor users, but those in charge ignored this. Furthermore, if Chinese-style properties are rebuilt, new landlords will inevitably demand the company install meters for each household according to the new contract schedule, requiring tenants to pay directly. The purchase price of these water meters and their maintenance costs will undoubtedly increase the social burden. It is true that water meters have been installed in Zhabei, the South, and the French Concession, but the situation is very different from the Public Settlement. In the other three areas, the packaged water system has not been in place for as long as it has in the Public Settlement. Furthermore, the other three companies would be unable to maintain balanced income and expenses without using the water meter system. The Public Settlement Waterworks Company has been highly profitable since its inception, enough to pay statutory dividends and more. Therefore, there is no need to specifically switch to the water meter system to cover expenses. The Waterworks Company's capital is in gold pounds, so there are insufficient dividends due to the excessive difference in the gold-silver exchange rate. However, whether the company can increase monthly prices because of this is questionable. The Public Works Department or society cannot force the company to change its gold capital to silver. Only shareholders have the right to decide this. This type of change would undoubtedly benefit users. Based on the above, revising water meter prices or setting graded price lists is insufficient to resolve this issue. The best solution is to give landlords and tenants one year to revise their contractual relationships so tenants become direct payers. During this year, old water prices should continue to apply. Once the habit of users paying directly is established, the meter installation fee per household, which is a major expense, should not be overlooked and should be carefully considered.

Letter to Tenants 108

The Real Estate Association believes the Waterworks Company's installation of master meters directly increases landlords' expenses, which will inevitably increase tenants' burdens. Their announcement is as follows: Tenant water usage should originally be paid for by tenants themselves. It is only for convenience that it is customary for landlords to collect and pay water fees within the rent. Originally, water fees only accounted for 5% of the rent, later increasing to 6%. In the nineteenth year of the Republic [1930], the British-owned Shanghai Waterworks Company demanded an additional 25% payment. The Shanghai Real Estate Association actively opposed this increase in water fees, as it directly increases landlords' expenses and inevitably increases tenants' burdens. This effort did not achieve its goal of cancellation. Our [waterworks] company uses water meters to calculate water fees, resulting in much higher fees than before, with some increasing up to ninefold. For example, with a monthly rent, the water fee was previously calculated at 7.5% of the rent, requiring only $1.50 per month. Now, calculated by meter, the water fee is $13.50 per month. Considering that tenants previously paid only $1.50 for water, they now have to pay $13.50. Thus, for a monthly rent of $20, in addition to the original water fee of $1.50, an additional $12 water fee must be paid. It is illogical and impractical for landlords to pay this water fee on behalf of tenants. The Shanghai Real Estate Association is actively opposing this, but the Waterworks Company insists on implementation and even threatens to cut off water. Landlords have advocated for tenants for a long time without success and can only explain to tenants that if tenants are willing to increase water fees, landlords should deduct the water fees collected within the rent, leaving tenants to manage it directly. If they are unwilling to increase water fees, they should work together to find a solution. Otherwise, landlords have no power to prevent the Waterworks Company from cutting off water and even less power to pay water fees on behalf of tenants because landlords must fully pay the Waterworks Company the water fees collected within the rent. This announcement is hereby issued for the public's information.

Yang Xingfo Explains the Anti-Imperialist League 111

And States the Situation of Inspecting Prisons in Beiping. According to a telegram from the National News Agency in Paris yesterday, the Non-War Association, organized by world celebrities, will form an investigation team to come to China to investigate the Northeast. Madame Sun Yat-sen, Soong Ching-ling, has already sent a telegram to welcome them. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency went to the Academia Sinica yesterday to meet with Vice President Yang Xingfo to inquire about the details and discuss the situation of inspecting prisons in Beiping.

Anti-Imperialist League According to Mr. Yang, the organization is actually named "Anti-Imperialist League." Madame Sun Yat-sen is one of the honorary presidents of the league. Participating countries include European, American, Chinese, and Indian nations. The major components include the Socialist Party and the Labour Party, mostly from the left-leaning side. All are world-renowned writers and scientists, holding significant positions and power. However, their names cannot be announced yet. Their purpose is to oppose any country's use of force to invade other countries, such as Japan's violent invasion of our Northeast. In particular, it is to oppose the alliance of imperialists to oppress weak countries. Therefore, during the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the league issued a lengthy statement condemning Japan's actions. However, our country did not disclose it at the time because it had not been translated. Recently, the league held an important meeting to discuss the "Non-Invasion of China Issue." Because the Lytton Commission report was produced by the hands of an imperialist group and contained many inaccuracies, they decided to form their own investigation team to come to China for investigation and compile another report to inform the world of the true situation. However, the date of their arrival in China is not known because their telegram has not been received. Madame Sun and others are preparing to receive them at that time.

The Process of Investigating Prisons Mr. Yang's inspection of prisons in Beiping was his first time. The results included the investigation of the Army Prison, the Military Branch's Reflection Center, and the Military Law Enforcement Detention Center. The Court Prison and the Public Security Bureau Detention Center were not investigated. There were over 150 detainees in these three prisons, mostly young students. After talking to them separately, it was found that only Han Linfu, the former communist believed to be dead, was around 40 years old. This person held a central position during the period of cooperation with the communists. The rest were around 20 to 30 years old. Half of them were detained due to communist suspicions during the separation of communists, and half were detained due to their relationship with the Revolutionary Relief Society. Among them, there was a girl, only 18 years old, also detained. In addition, there was one person with special circumstances. The prison buildings were converted from factories due to economic constraints. They were crude and simple, with 16 people in one room, which was extremely unsanitary. Compared to the model prisons, they were worlds apart and urgently needed improvement. Future investigations have not been decided yet, but experts will be invited to join the investigation in the future.

Reasons for Obstructing Ancient Artifacts Continuing, he said that the 120 boxes of ancient artifacts transported from the Academia Sinica to Shanghai were different from the ancient artifacts of the Palace Museum. The ancient artifacts of the Academia Sinica were turtle shells, pottery shards, and bronzes, excavated from the soil in Zhengzhou. Most of them were incomplete and only used for historical research. The southward transport of the ancient artifacts of the Palace Museum was originally to avoid danger. People in Beiping believed that these ancient artifacts were essential for the prosperity of Beiping. Once removed, it would be affected. Therefore, they strongly opposed it. After boxing them up, the porters and rickshaw pullers refused to transport them for fear of being blamed by the locals, leading to obstruction. As for the rumors of selling ancient artifacts, it was another form of propaganda. Therefore, in the end, the people of Beiping hoped that after the dangerous period passed, they would still be transported back to Beiping for preservation. After Yi Peiji and others inquired to President Song, Mr. Song replied by telegram, promising to transport them back to Beiping when the city was stable. It is hoped that this telegram will prevent obstruction. This is the general situation I know.

The Ministry of Railways is grabbing land in the Pengpu area to build a joint transportation station. After consultations among the Ministries of Interior, Industry, Railways, and Military Affairs, the original plan remains unchanged. The villagers of the area submitted another petition to the Executive Yuan yesterday, requesting reconsideration. The document stated, "Submitting this to request reconsideration of the land grab for the joint transportation station because the decision of the four ministries' consultation is still unfair. According to reports in the Shanghai newspaper, the land grab issue for the joint transportation station between the Zhenru and Pengpu areas has been decided by a meeting of the Ministries of Interior, Military Affairs, Industry, and Railways, and the original plan of the Ministry of Railways will be carried out. Building a station in the Pengpu area is impractical and does not conform to general academic theory. We have already prepared detailed reports and illustrations to request to avoid this. Unexpectedly, this time the ministries' meeting did not change the plan and did not consider the actual situation and the hardships of the people. National construction cannot be based solely on the perspective of the authorities and become an arbitrary iron case. This is the second reason why we should follow the people's will and reconsider. The Zhenru area has ceded over 1,400 mu of open space, and the Pengpu area has added over 700 mu of village households. Where is the sufficient reason for ceding on one side and adding on the other? The Ministry of Railways has never clearly indicated this. This is the third reason why we should carefully consider and reconsider. The Ministry of Railways said that the joint transportation station occupies an area of 2,800 mu, but the staked boundary reaches over 4,000 mu. How will the remaining land be disposed of? This has not been clearly announced. This is the fourth reason why we should plan in detail and reconsider. Based on the above reasons, we dare to submit this document again to request review, order the relevant ministries to conduct a thorough reconsideration, and provide a satisfactory answer to each of the points presented. Otherwise, this concerns the lives and property of the people, and we vow not to recognize it. This urgent plea is submitted to Acting President of the Executive Yuan Song."
