Bandits Attempt Robbery and Open Fire on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway 121

Bandit Li Shunfa Escapes but is Recaptured

Soldier Wu Nairu Sacrifices His Life in the Line of Duty

At the 31st bridge on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway between Songjiang and Shihudang, there is a sentry post of soldiers from the 12th Company of the 3rd Battalion of the 2nd Regiment of the Jiangsu Security Force (the regimental headquarters is stationed in Songjiang). On the night before last (the 5th), around 6:00 PM, soldier Wu Nairu of the bridge sentry post apprehended a bandit and confiscated a short gun converted from a rifle and a row of bullets. Unexpectedly, around 11:00 PM that night, a large gang of more than 20 bandits suddenly arrived and opened fire on the bridge sentry post, intending to rob it and rescue the captured bandit. Both sides exchanged fire as if facing a major enemy. After about 15 minutes, the bandits, unable to withstand the pressure, fled, fatally wounding security force soldier Wu Nairu. The details are as follows:

Black-Clad Vanguard: The sentry post of soldiers from the 3rd Battalion of the 2nd Regiment of the Security Force at the 31st bridge on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway between Songjiang and Shihudang, consisting of about 11 soldiers, was approached by a man dressed in short black clothes around 6:00 PM on the (5th). His appearance was suspicious, and he headed straight for the 31st bridge. Sentry Wu Nairu spotted him and immediately intercepted him with his gun, inspecting him. He found a short gun converted from a rifle and a row of bullets concealed on the man's body. The bandit did not resist and was immediately apprehended and taken to the sentry post under the bridge for temporary detention, intending to be sent to the Songjiang regimental headquarters for interrogation the next morning. The bandit was taken to the sentry post and briefly interrogated by the platoon leader. The bandit confessed to the name Li Shunfa, age 28, from Ningbo, and admitted without hesitation to conspiring with a gang to commit robbery. Due to the lateness of the hour, he was not sent to the Songjiang regimental headquarters but was temporarily bound with hemp rope and detained. Attempt to Seize the Bandit Leader: Unexpectedly, around 11:00 PM that night, about 120 meters west of the bridge, a large gang of more than 20 bandits was suddenly discovered. They lined up and opened fire on the bridge sentry post, as if facing a major enemy, intending to rescue the captured bandit leader, Li Shunfa. At that time, all the soldiers at the bridge sentry post fought back bravely. Both sides exchanged fire for about 15 minutes. As a result, the bandits were unable to withstand the pressure and fled. However, bridge guard soldier Wu Nairu was shot in the right chest by the bandits and died on the spot.

Biting the Rope and Jumping into the River: Li Shunfa, the detained bandit, took advantage of the firefight to bite through the rope binding him with his teeth and escaped. He jumped into the river to flee, but was spotted by the sentry, who wounded him in the head and recaptured him. He was taken back to the sentry post for detention.

A Suspect: Around 5:00 AM on the morning of the (6th), the bridge sentry was searching in the vicinity and apprehended a suspect. The suspect confessed to the name Wu Chengjun, age 34, from Anhui, wearing a gray cloth military uniform. He claimed to be a discharged soldier who, lacking travel expenses, planned to walk along the railway line to Shanghai to return home. The sentry immediately sent the wounded bandit Li Shunfa and the suspect Wu Chengjun to the Songjiang Second Security Regiment headquarters for interrogation yesterday morning at 7:00 AM. Meanwhile, soldier Wu Nairu, who was shot and killed by the bandits, was prepared for burial in a coffin.

Military Police Deployed: Police Chief Wang of the South Station Police Team of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, based on a report from the Shihudang Railway Police, immediately dispatched nearby railway police to assist the bridge sentry in rounding up the bandits. He also led senior police officers and inspectors to investigate the scene to report to the two railway police departments for investigation. The bridges along the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway line are vital to transportation and are of utmost importance. The fact that these bandits dared to be so rampant is indeed disruptive to travelers. After investigation, the 31st bridge is guarded by a sentry post of soldiers from the 12th Company of the 3rd Battalion of the 2nd Regiment of the Jiangsu Security Force, and the 34th bridge is currently guarded by two water police patrol boats. However, the remaining 30th, 38th, and 43rd bridges, as well as the Shihudang area, have no military presence, only railway police patrolling. The police force is weak. The railway police chief has not only dispatched additional railway police to guard these bridges but has also sent a letter from the railway bureau to the military units stationed in each area, requesting them to dispatch troops to guard them in order to strengthen the force and ensure transportation.

Public Concession Plans to Implement Mandatory Registration of Doctors 122

The Public Concession's Municipal Council has been deliberating for years on the mandatory registration of practicing physicians in the concession. In 1925, based on the report of the Poison Investigation Committee, the Health Department formally recommended this matter. However, as the Municipal Council did not yet have the legislative power for this mandatory registration, it was not immediately implemented. However, to protect the public and gradually eliminate unqualified doctors, a voluntary registration system was established in 1931 under the supervision of the Shanghai Medical Committee. The names, qualifications, nationalities, etc., of voluntarily registered physicians, dentists, and veterinarians were compiled into a register and published. This register has been published twice, in August 1931 and July 1932. The third edition of the register is currently being printed, which includes 606 physicians, 115 dentists, 14 veterinarians, and 33 traditional Chinese medicine practitioners. Those listed in the register are registered doctors recognized by the Shanghai Medical Committee. Recently, public opinion has held that the implementation of mandatory registration cannot be delayed any further. The last Shanghai Medical Committee meeting resolved to request the Municipal Council to proceed with this matter as soon as possible. The majority of members believe that without mandatory registration, the malpractice of incompetent doctors and the rampant advertising, etc., cannot be dealt with. Furthermore, given that the Shanghai Municipal Government and the French Concession both have mandatory registration measures, the Public Concession cannot delay any longer. The Municipal Council's Health Committee has expressed its approval in principle of this proposal and will soon submit it to the Board of Directors for a decision. Many taxpayers have also submitted opinion letters on this matter.

Two Robbers and Murderers Sentenced to Death 123

Wang Zhongde and Sun Lianfu Both Sentenced to Death

Han Sen Sentenced to Fourteen Years of Imprisonment

Wang Zhongde, also known as Chun Si, age 33, from Anhui, became acquainted with the wife of a friend, surnamed Yao, the year before last winter. Later, during the war in Zhabei, he colluded with a fellow villager named Little Liu to secretly assassinate Yao. Afterwards, Little Liu frequently demanded money from Wang for expenses. On the evening of July 20th last year, around 9:00 PM, Wang, deeply resenting him, entrusted Sun Lianfu (also known as Little Lianfu), age 19, and Han Sen (also known as Little Lao Han) to each carry a handgun to the entrance of Jixiang Lane on Yulin Road. Taking advantage of Little Liu sleeping on a canvas chair enjoying the cool air, they shot him in the head, killing him. After the incident, Wang and the other three were successively apprehended by Chinese Detective Lu Gengsheng of the Yulin Road Police Station. It was found that Sun Lianfu and Han Sen had, between June 6th and July 19th last year, formed a gang and used weapons to rob Chen Guozhi at No. 60 Fenzhou Road and Chen Qingsong at No. 342 Yangzhou Road, among other two households' property. A handgun and seven bullets were also seized from the house at No. 41 Qiwupu Road, and together with the suspect Ouyang Shilong, also from Anhui, they were handed over to the First Special District Local Court. After repeated investigations, a date was set for the pronouncement of the verdict, the details of which have been reported in the newspapers. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan took the bench in the Third Criminal Court and announced the verdict. The defendant Wang Zhongde (aka Chun Si) was sentenced to death for the crime of jointly premeditating murder, with permanent deprivation of civil rights. Sun Lianfu (aka Little Lianfu) was sentenced to death for the crime of jointly premeditating murder, with permanent deprivation of civil rights, and sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for the crime of armed robbery by a gang of three or more people. The death sentence was to be executed. Han Sen (aka Little Lao Han) was sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for the crime of aiding and abetting premeditated murder, with ten years of deprivation of civil rights, and sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for the crime of armed robbery by a gang of three or more people, to be executed for fourteen years, with ten years of deprivation of civil rights. The number of days of pre-trial detention was to be counted as two days for one day. Ouyang Shilong was sentenced to a fine of one hundred yuan for the crime of privately possessing military firearms and ammunition. If unable to pay the fine, he would serve one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The firearms and ammunition were confiscated.

Thugs and Local Bullies Impersonate Detectives to Investigate Cigarettes 124

Taking Advantage of the Opportunity to Extort Money and Commit All Kinds of Evil Deeds

Several Cases Have Been Verified

In recent years, the Public Concession authorities have been strictly cracking down on the cigarette ban within the concession. This anti-smoking work is all handled by the specially established Narcotics Division. Since its establishment, it has achieved remarkable results. Therefore, regardless of the size of the smoking case, such as private trafficking of opium, setting up smoking dens, etc., there is hardly a day without it in the First Special Court. However, there is a group of unemployed thugs who take advantage of this time to impersonate detectives from the Narcotics Division, etc., to extort money from residents within the concession. There are several cases of victims every day. Recently, the Narcotics Division learned of this and conducted a thorough investigation. On the 16th of last month, they apprehended the criminals Zhang Shunchang, Xu Yuangui, Lu Ronggui, and Wu Shiqing, who were extorting money under this pretense, in Room 20 of the Aido Hotel on Aidoa Road. Letters, flashlights, batteries, and other items were seized. They were handed over to the First Special District Court for questioning. Because the police were investigating, the discussion was changed to a later date. This has been reported in this newspaper. Now, Song Bingzheng, Chen Yaoting, and West Detective Mai Fei, who are handling this case in the Narcotics Division, have found that the defendants have committed nine cases of extorting silver dollars from residents in the concession under the guise of police detectives from November of last year to the time of their arrest this year. 1) On January 6th of this year, they extorted 20 yuan from the Xu Jianquan family at No. 563 Pike Road under the pretext of searching for opium. 2) On November 19th of last year, they extorted 80 yuan from Li Mei at No. 129 Back Road. 3) On November 20th of last year, they extorted 5 yuan from Du Quefeng at No. 14 Xinzha Road. 4) On December 25th of last year, they extorted 10 yuan from Wang Li at No. 137 Back Road. 5) On November 20th of last year, they extorted 50 yuan from Qian Wu at No. 8 Xinping Lane, Longmen Road. 6) On November 13th of last year, they extorted 200 yuan from Jing Shiyuan at No. 954 Broadway Road. 7) On December 30th of last year, they extorted 75 yuan from Wang Yuzhang at No. 93 Fujian Road. 8) On November 28th of last year, they extorted 300 yuan from Fei Lianshi and Xu Chunchu at No. 276 Shandong Road. 9) On November 20th of last year, they extorted 50 yuan from Zhang Liu at No. 64 Shandong Road. Yesterday morning, they were handed over to the Second Criminal Court of the Special Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang requested a special hearing at a later date due to the large number of witnesses in this case. Judge Qian Wenqi approved the request and ordered that the case be heard again tomorrow afternoon (i.e., today). In addition, the Narcotics Division recently apprehended a criminal named Fan Debiao and seized a pair of handcuffs, which were brought to the police station. It was found that Fan was also one of the gang of thugs who extorted money. On September 25th of last year, he broke into the house of Chen Heshang, a resident at No. 142 Shanxi Road, claiming to be a detective sent by the police to investigate opium. He found smoking paraphernalia and, as a result, extorted 4 yuan. Therefore, Chen Heshang was summoned to testify against Fan Debiao yesterday morning and handed over to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. According to police lawyer Wang Yaotang's statement of the case, there have been many cases of impersonating detectives to extort money recently, which has made it difficult for Narcotics Division detectives to handle cases. He requested that the defendant be severely punished to deter others from following suit. According to Chen Heshang's testimony, Fan Debiao's confession was evasive, and he hired lawyer Li Fengshen to defend him in court. Judge Qian verified the confession and sentenced Fan Debiao to four months of imprisonment for the crime of extortion.

An Old Thief, With No Hope of Getting Out of Prison, Resorts to His Old Tricks the Day After His Release 125

The Number of Theft Cases Committed in His Life is Countless

He Has Been Apprehended and Punished Fifteen Times

Around 2:00 AM on the morning of the day before yesterday, the residence of a Westerner, Hai Qiawan, at No. 257 Columbia Road in West Shanghai, was visited by a thief who pried open the door and entered. As Mr. Hai was out at the time, the thief was able to go upstairs and into the room, stealing gold and silver utensils worth 530 yuan and carrying the loot out. But feeling unsatisfied, he hid the stolen goods in a nearby wasteland and returned to Mr. Hai's bedroom, intending to steal other items. Just then, Mr. Hai returned home and saw a dark figure in the room. He shouted, "Who is there?" But received no answer. Realizing it was a criminal, he was about to arrest him when the thief jumped out of the window and fled. Mr. Hai drew his own handgun and fired three shots, but missed. The thief managed to escape with the loot. Mr. Hai reported the incident to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which notified all police stations to be on the lookout. Unfortunately, the thief's luck ran out. While carrying the loot and passing through the intersection of Zhapu Road and Tiantong Road in Hongkou around 9:00 AM, he was spotted by a Chinese constable from No. 618 Police Station, who apprehended him. When questioned about the origin of the items in his bag, he confessed that they were stolen. He was taken to the police station and transferred to the Jing'an Temple Police Station. Chinese Detective Yang Xinzheng investigated and found his name to be Jiang Deming, a native of Shanghai, age 42 (also known as Lin Deren, Jiang Derun, Zhang Shisheng, and You Asheng). Stealing was his regular occupation. The number of theft cases he had committed in his life was countless. He had been apprehended and punished as many as fifteen times. This time, he had just been released from the Caohejing Prison in the interior on the 4th of this month, and on the 5th, he was arrested again for theft. He could be called an old thief. Yesterday morning, the police handed Jiang over to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the above situation and requested that he be severely punished. The Westerner Hai Qiawan also sent a representative to the court to testify that all the items retrieved by the police were indeed the original stolen goods. When questioned, Jiang Deming bowed his head and remained silent. Judge Qian Wenqi verified the confession and sentenced Jiang Deming to two years of imprisonment for the crime of habitual theft. The stolen goods were to be returned to the original owner for collection.

Restoration of Wusong Telephone Service 126

Work Started Yesterday

The Wusong telephone service has not been restored since the January 28th Incident. The original commercial Songyang Telephone Company was completely destroyed and suffered heavy losses, and has gone bankrupt. The Wusong municipal authorities and the Chamber of Commerce believe that the lack of telephone service in Songjiang for a long time not only hinders communication but also greatly affects local security. Therefore, they have repeatedly sent letters to the Shanghai Department of Transportation Telephone Bureau to handle the matter. The bureau already had a branch office on Guizi Road in Wusong, specializing in the Songjiang-Shanghai long-distance telephone line. It is now known that the bureau dispatched Engineer Xu yesterday, leading more than 20 workers and transporting a large amount of materials to Songjiang, to rush to erect poles and lines for the entire Wusong area. It is estimated that it will take three weeks to complete the work.

New Launch of the Seaport Quarantine Station Named Hua Tuo 127

The Zi Lin Newspaper reports that the National Seaport Quarantine Station added a new motor launch today (the 6th), named Hua Tuo. The boat is 56 feet long, 11 feet wide, and 6 feet 9 inches deep, with a speed of 8 miles per hour. It is equipped with a Schneider-Diesel engine, between 55 and 65 horsepower, with three cylinders rotating 550 to 625 times per minute. This launch was originally intended to be assigned to the Wusongkou to pick up and drop off medical officers boarding and disembarking from ships. Now, due to the busy inspection work in the Huangpu River, the original launch is not sufficient, so it is temporarily used in the Huangpu River.

New Discovery of Radio 128

Stove as Radio Receiver

On the north side of the upper floor of the Science Hall of the Jiangsu Provincial Education Institute in Wuxi, there is a radio broadcasting station. On the south side of the lower floor (separated by about six or seven feet), there is an agricultural laboratory with a stove inside. When broadcasting, a sound is emitted from the stove, and the sound is quite clear, like the small speaker of a third-class radio. A certain gentleman in the institute is currently studying it, and it is hoped that domestic experts will also study it together so that there may be inventions in the future.

Qingpu Vessel Aground at Taizi Shoal 129

Vessel Sends Telegraph Requesting Assistance: The river has been very shallow recently, and the retreat of the river near Taizi Shoal, Anqing, is even worse. The Sanbei Company's Fengpu vessel ran aground on the 26th of last month. The bureau dispatched a ship to tow it for three days before it was pulled out. It is currently coming from Datong with coal and has not yet arrived in Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon, the company received a telegram from the Qingpu vessel, stating that the ship, traveling east from Hankou, ran aground again on the Jiangmian of Taizi Shoal the night before last (i.e., the 5th) due to shallow water. The Qingpu was loaded with many goods and passengers, so the hull was trapped in the sand and mud, and the vessel could not move.

Awakened Lion's Rescue Ineffective: After the Qingpu vessel ran aground, it immediately sent a wireless telegram for help. The company's upstream Yangtze River vessel, the Awakened Lion, received the telegram and immediately sailed to tow it. When the Awakened Lion arrived at Taizi Shoal, the water was still shallow, and it could not get close to the Qingpu. It used an iron cable to connect to the Qingpu vessel, and the Awakened Lion tried its best to tow it. The Qingpu also reversed the engines, but as the Qingpu vessel was heavily loaded with cargo and the draft was deep, it was stuck firmly. The Awakened Lion's rescue was unsuccessful.

Changxing Towing Barge to Tow: The only way to rescue it now is to unload part of the cargo from each cabin of the Qingpu to reduce the draft, and to transfer a batch of passengers first, and then tow it again when the tide rises. After discussion, the Qingpu shipowner telegraphed the Hankou branch to order the Changjiang downstream vessel, Changxing, to bring a towing barge and rush to Taizi Shoal to unload the Qingpu cargo in order to tow it. Hankou replied to Shanghai, approving the dispatch of the Changxing and towing barge to rescue it.

Renaming of Jardine Matheson's Upriver Vessel 130

Qinghe Renamed Xinchanghe

Jardine Matheson's Qinghe vessel, which runs on the upriver Yichang-Chongqing line, ran aground downstream of Chongqing last month. The bottom of the ship was slightly damaged, so it came to Shanghai for repairs. The work has now been completed. The company has changed the name of the vessel to Xinchanghe. The procedures for changing the name and customs vessel license have also been completed. It is scheduled to depart from Shanghai tomorrow evening (the 8th) with cargo and passengers, heading directly to Chongqing.

Young Woman Bravely Pursues Thieves Who Stole Tuition Fees 135

Yu Jinmao, 52 years old, from Shaoxing Yaoxian, has been running Hengde Coal Store at No. 175 Fuyou Road, inside the New North Gate of this city, for 22 years. Yu's wife, Shao, 48 years old, lives upstairs in the store. They have a son and a daughter. The eldest son, Weiliang, 24 years old, is a student at Guanghua University and is about to graduate this semester. He is married to Mao. The younger daughter, Xinggen, 19 years old, is studying at the Shanghai High School. Because Yu has been ill, Shao assists with the daily store business and also manages over thirty rental properties on Daxing Street, near the Small West Gate, collecting rent monthly. The couple works diligently and thriftily, and their business is doing well, with some savings accumulated. This has attracted the attention of thieves. At about 7:00 PM yesterday, just after Yu and his family finished dinner, five thieves, armed with two handguns and a dagger, broke into the store, brandished their weapons, and threatened them not to make a sound. They drove the shop owner and his family into a room to monitor their movements. The other robbers rushed upstairs and robbed them of 350 silver dollars, about 50 dollars' worth of copper coins, a gold watch, a gold pocket watch, three gold bracelets, a gold chain, and two gold rings. After the robbery, they took the stolen goods and fled out the door, escaping towards Zhangchuan Lane, inside the New North Gate. Shao immediately reported the incident to the patrol police at the Second Precinct of the First District. Meanwhile, Yu's daughter followed the thieves, tracking them to a dark alley next to Jishan Temple on Jishan Street. The thieves threatened her, so she dared not go further and stopped the pursuit, returning home. Afterwards, Precinct Chief Xu Chenghuang received the report and led police to surround and search the area, but the thieves had long since fled without a trace. The case was reported to the General Bureau for record and assistance in the investigation. Director Wen, upon receiving the report, sent personnel to investigate the scene and ordered the detective captain, Lu Yingxun, to have the stationed detectives inquire about clues from the victims. According to reports, the silver dollars were intended to pay for the children's tuition fees today. The daughter, knowing that her tuition fees had been robbed and that she might not be able to continue her studies, bravely pursued the robbers. However, the eldest son is near graduation, and it would be a pity for him to drop out. The entire family is dejected, a heartbreaking scene to witness.

Shanghai Public Safety Bureau Issues New Measures for Handling Transiting Refugees 136

Orders Distributed to All Districts and Precincts Yesterday

Refugees from various regions come to Shanghai seeking food every day. Some cunning ones often return after being sent away, regarding fraudulently obtaining rations as a lucrative business. The Municipal Public Safety Bureau believes that if such situations are not strictly controlled, it will not only tarnish the city's image but also easily affect public safety. Therefore, it has formulated four measures for handling transiting refugees and distributed them to all districts and precincts yesterday. The original order and measures are as follows:

Order: Regarding the matter of issuing orders, this city is commercially prosperous and has convenient transportation. Refugees from various regions come here seeking food every day. Whenever refugees enter the city, the district or precinct in charge immediately telegrams the point of origin or directly informs the Social Affairs Bureau to transfer aid to charitable organizations for issuing rations. Then, the district or precinct in charge escorts them out of the city. However, there is a lack of communication between the parties, and there is no detailed registration of the refugees' entry and exit points for investigation. As a result, some refugees receive rations in Pudong in the morning and seek food in the South City in the evening, moving back and forth within Shanghai. This situation, where they are driven away from one place only to move to another, is endless. This can seriously affect public safety and, to a lesser extent, harm the city's image. Therefore, four measures for handling transiting refugees and a reporting form are hereby established. In addition to sending a letter to the Social Affairs Bureau to inform all charitable organizations that after rations are issued, they must notify this bureau for verification. Besides distributing this notice, the aforementioned measures and reporting form are attached and issued with this order. The district and precinct chiefs are ordered to strictly comply and implement them. This is of utmost importance. Respectfully, this order. February 6th, 1933, Director Wen Hongen.

Measures: 1. When refugees enter the city, the district or precinct in charge shall immediately telegram the bureau and quickly find a temporary residence address and send police to guard them, preventing them from moving freely or forcibly soliciting on the streets. Once a charitable organization issues rations, the district or precinct in charge shall immediately send police to escort them out of the city limits and quickly fill out a report form to be sent to the bureau for record. 2. If a district or precinct verifies, through the refugee's residence permit or other means, that the refugees have already received rations, they must be escorted out of the city. 3. If refugees must pass through the territory of another district or precinct when leaving the city, and it is deemed necessary to continue to send police, the district or precinct in charge may directly discuss the measures via telegram. The district or precinct in charge must not shirk responsibility or refuse to send police. 4. If it is found that any district or precinct intentionally delays, causing refugees to stay in their territory for a long time, the responsible officers of the district or precinct in charge will be severely punished. If it is found that any precinct performs well and has made meritorious contributions, the responsible department may submit a request for review and reward.

Coal and Firewood Workers Petition Party and Government Agencies Yesterday 137

Objecting to Employers' Unjustified Dismissal of Employees

Several stores in the city's coal industry, including Yuansheng, dismissed dozens of employees, including Yu Zhicheng, during the Lunar New Year. The workers reported the matter to the labor union, which sent representatives to mediate, but to no avail. They immediately submitted a petition to the party and government agencies, requesting assistance. The Municipal Party Department sent representatives to mediate and decided that the stores should not expel the workers from the stores before a resolution is reached. The dismissed workers went to the stores the day before yesterday to await a resolution. However, Yuansheng Coal and Charcoal Company requested the Public Safety Bureau to send plainclothes detective Fang Chao to prevent this and detained seven people, including Yu Huifeng, director of the labor union, and Yu Zhicheng, the worker, at the Fourth District Public Safety Bureau. They were released because there were no charges against them. The workers were enraged, and yesterday they sent more than ten representatives, including Li Hua, Zheng Xiaotang, and Hu Chuchao, to the Municipal Party Department with a petition. Lu Yinchu, a staff member of the Civil Affairs Department, received them and, after inquiring about their intentions, promised to coordinate with the Social Affairs Bureau to mediate. They then went to the Social Affairs Bureau to make the same request, asking for practical assistance to maintain the workers' livelihoods.

The Tongru Chonghai Qi Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, upon receiving news of the Lyusi Mutiny, convened a meeting of the Executive Supervisory Committee at the association's office at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than twenty committee members, including Mao Huiru, attended. Chairman Mao chaired the meeting. After discussing the Lyusi Mutiny, they decided to send telegrams to the province and county requesting them to send troops to suppress the mutiny and to send a letter to the Lyusi Chamber of Commerce inquiring about the details of the mutineers' looting and the extent of the damage, in order to properly discuss the aftermath. The original telegrams are recorded below:

To the Provincial Government: To Governor Gu, Chairman of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government, and to Zhao, Director of the Civil Affairs Department, and Han Jun, Director of the Security Department: The garrison guerrilla troops in the Lyusi District of Tong Prefecture suddenly mutinied on the 豔 day, looting both towns, causing great losses, killing three people including Chen Zhixi, and abducting many men and women, fleeing by sea. The news of the alarm has spread, and we are shocked. In recent years, Tong Prefecture has been repeatedly harassed by pirates and ravaged by bandits. The city is desolate, and the people's livelihoods are impoverished. The wounds are deep, and the pain is immense. Just when we were hoping to recuperate and breathe, unfortunately, a mutiny broke out in the heart of the land, causing another disaster. The suffering is unimaginable. These mutinying troops were originally pirates who were recruited and reorganized. Their ambitions are difficult to tame. Now that they have rebelled and become bandits, their ferocity is fully revealed. We believe that they should be completely suppressed and not allowed to flee far away. Otherwise, the troops will come and the bandits will go, and the bandits will come when the troops leave. The past of Pan Sang can serve as a warning. The people of this association in Shanghai are deeply concerned about their hometown and are filled with grief. We dare to telegram you, Your Excellency, requesting you to send capable naval vessels to the area and strictly order County Magistrate Zhang to supervise the local police force and jointly suppress the mutiny on land and sea. With the determination to eliminate evil, we seek a long-term solution and fundamentally eliminate the problem, preventing it from spreading. Please order County Magistrate Zhang to rescue and properly settle all the abducted people and affected households, so as to stabilize the local area and reassure the people. We anxiously await your orders. Tongru Chonghai Qi Fellow-Provincials Association respectfully bows. To County Magistrate Zhang, Nantong: To County Magistrate Zhang of Nantong, and to the Liaison Defense Office and the Security Committee: We have just learned that the garrison guerrilla troops in the Lyusi District suddenly mutinied, looting both towns, causing great losses, killing three people including Chen Fuzhixi, and abducting many men and women, fleeing by sea, and so on. The news of the alarm has spread, and we are shocked. In recent years, the county has been repeatedly harassed by bandits and pirates, causing deep wounds. The vitality has not yet recovered. Commerce is currently in a state of decline, and the countryside is facing bankruptcy. Just when the people are exhausted and hoping to recuperate and breathe, unexpectedly, a mutiny broke out in the heart of the land, causing another disaster. The suffering is unbearable. The people of this association in Shanghai are deeply concerned about their hometown and are filled with grief. We dare to telegram you, Your Excellency, requesting you to supervise the local police force and urgently dispatch land and naval forces to jointly suppress the mutiny. We also request you to consult with neighboring counties to strictly prevent and block the mutineers, ensuring that they are all wiped out and not allowed to flee and spread, so as to eliminate hidden dangers. Please investigate and rescue all the abducted people and affected households, so as to stabilize the local area and reassure the people. We anxiously await your prayers. Tongru Chonghai Qi Fellow-Provincials Association respectfully bows.

Shanghai-Nanjing Railway's Second Express Train Suffers Engine Damage Yesterday Morning 139

The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway's Second Special Express Train, which departed from Nanjing at 10:00 AM yesterday, suffered a broken axle on its engine at around 12:30 PM when it was passing through Xinfeng Station, causing it to be unable to move forward or backward. Another engine was used to tow the Second Special Express Train, which departed from Xinfeng at 3:25 PM, with a delay of more than two hours. General Management Office Meeting of Various Insurance Industries 141

The Second Board Meeting Held Yesterday Approved the Business Regulations

The General Management Office of Various Insurance Industries in this city, with the aim of promoting Chinese merchant insurance business and safeguarding the interests of policyholders, is scheduled to open on the tenth of this month. Yesterday afternoon, the management office held its second board meeting, chaired by Chairman Wang Yansong. First, General Manager Fang Jiaobo reported on the preparation process and recent progress. Then, the meeting discussed the business plan and the progress of the procedure, and the following business regulations were approved: (Article 1) This management office manages various insurance businesses on behalf of Chinese merchant insurance companies. The types are as follows: 1. Marine insurance, 2. Fire insurance, 3. Life insurance, 4. Automobile insurance, 5. Accident insurance, 6. Others. The insured company for the above insurance types will be determined according to the policyholder's designation. (Article 2) This management office handles insurance business with the following items: 1. Improving the reputation of Chinese merchant insurance industry, 2. Studying the improvement of insurance industry, 3. Increasing Chinese merchant insurance business, 4. Investigating the situation of insurance industry, 5. Statistics of insurance industry business, 6. Promoting the importance of insurance industry, 7. Answering inquiries about insurance matters. (Article 3) The insurance handled by this management office on behalf of policyholders, such as in the event of a disaster, the management office shall represent the policyholder in handling all procedures and collect a handling fee, which shall be set at 1% of the actual income. (Article 4) The policyholders entrusted to this management office shall enjoy the following benefits: 1. Simple procedures, 2. Fair prices, 3. Reducing accidental losses, 4. Selecting reputable companies, 5. Handling claim procedures, 6. Enjoying legitimate protection, 7. Eliminating the cost of socialising, 8. Collecting claims on behalf of the policyholder and eliminating the effort of travelling. (Article 5) For all types of insurance managed by this management office, the insurance policies issued by each company shall be collected and transferred to the policyholder by this management office, and the premiums shall also be collected and remitted to the company by this management office. (Article 6) Chinese merchant insurance companies that wish to expand their business may enter into special agreements with this management office. (Article 7) In addition to directly managing insurance business, all trade associations and individuals may contact this management office to establish branch offices or serve as managers. (Article 8) Insurance managed by branch offices or managers must be handled in accordance with the Manager Regulations established by this management office. (Article 9) All external documents and receipts of this management office shall be signed by the general and deputy managers. (Article 10) The business affairs of this management office, in addition to being decided by the general and deputy managers, shall be handled by the business department. (Article 11) These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Board of Directors, and the same shall apply to amendments.

『Elopement』or『Suicide』? 148

丨A Letter from Mr. Hong Huaide丨

I read your newspaper's reader advisory column every day, and it has indirectly solved many of my problems. However, sometimes I have difficult issues of a different nature. I have repeatedly wanted to ask you, but I worry that your newspaper will think my ideas are immature and not answer me. Now I have a life-or-death problem. Please guide me, sir. I am twenty years old this year. Because of my family's poverty, I stopped attending school six years ago! I now work as a clerk in a small department store, and my monthly salary is meager, only enough for my personal expenses. When I was in elementary school before, there was a female classmate three years younger than me who was close to me. Later, her family moved to Jiangxi Province for a few years, so we both forgot about each other. By chance, last year they moved near my store. We met again after a long separation, and our feelings deepened. Sometimes I take time to chat with her in the countryside, and our love has gradually grown stronger. Our ambitions, ages, and appearances are quite compatible, but it is a pity that our family backgrounds are too different! She is the sixth young lady from a middle-class family, and I am a struggling young man with no clear future, with absolutely no one to rely on except myself. In the old-fashioned society, who doesn't see "raising a daughter to marry into a high-ranking family"? Her father will definitely not abandon the concept of marrying someone of equal social status and marry her to a struggling young man like me! Half a year ago, her parents had already betrothed her to a so-called young boss. She resisted desperately, but to no avail. As a result, she has become increasingly thin. I always try to comfort her. I am also disliked by the store owner, and I am forced by circumstances to distance myself from her! She was extremely angry and attempted suicide, intending to show her love for me. Fortunately, her family discovered it, and she was able to recover. As for me, I ask myself in the quiet night, and I really feel sorry for her dedication! I am determined to elope with her regardless, but firstly, it would violate the law, and secondly, it would implicate her father's reputation. After thinking it over, the only way out for us is suicide! Sir, you are experienced and knowledgeable, enough to shed light on my dark room. Besides death, is there any other solution?

Answer: After reading your letter, I cannot help but shed a tear of sympathy for you first. Your problem is a common problem for young people in modern society. Our newspaper's "advisory" service to readers is dedicated to providing sincere and intelligent advice.

As for the limited knowledge and experience of our colleagues, we will openly discuss and research. There is no shortage of enlightened and insightful people in the country, and they will surely be able to teach you. Your fear that we would not answer because of "immature thoughts" is indeed a misunderstanding. This is what we should solemnly declare to you before answering your letter. We have a basic concept regarding the relationship between men and women, which is that we express extreme sympathy for any relationship, including love, that is entirely built on the foundation of "mutual consent" and "mutual understanding." However, the so-called "mutual consent and mutual understanding" must have a necessary condition: that both parties must have a considerable period of mutual observation. During this observation period, both parties must use their reason, knowledge, and experience to analyze each other's temperament, habits, ability to earn a living, and plans for future cohabitation. Never act rashly based on temporary blind emotions: "Suicide" is definitely not the solution: "Elopement" is also not a good idea. Why? ㈠ Lack of freedom in marriage is an inevitable phenomenon in the current social system. Because of the lack of freedom in marriage, we should actively attack the society that makes it unfree, that is the mark of a hero. Suicide is a surrender and retreat to this unfree society. Although it is euphemistically called passive resistance, it is actually ending it all with death. Wouldn't that be laughed at by those who know better? Even if you die, it wouldn't count as a brave ghost, so we fundamentally oppose suicide. ㈡ "Elopement" is originally possible under the following conditions: (A) Both people have a very thorough understanding of the future and see that there are endless difficulties and dangers and vow to fight to the end: (B) Both people have considerable experience in society, so that they will not be at a loss as soon as they leave the door; (C) Both Yuan Cheng · Tao Mu · Huang Bodu · Shen Yu · Ji An · Ping · Li Zikuan · Jiang Ji Hu · Zu · both families, totaling more than a hundred people, after the wedding hosts from both sides gave speeches, the guests unanimously elected Xu Shiying to give a speech on behalf of them, and the wedding was concluded. The bridegroom is currently studying in the Department of Mechanical Engineering at Jiaotong University, and the bride is a top student at Nanjing Huiwen Girls' Middle School. Mr. Zhai has lived in Suhu for generations, and he and Mr. Hu were comrades in adversity more than thirty years ago. During the Qing Dynasty's Guangxu years, Mr. Hu and Mr. Zhai jointly established agricultural reclamation in Wanqing Lake, using military methods to control farmers and tenants, in order to restore the old order. At that time, Su Manshu and Liu Guanghan taught at Anhui Public School, and Chen Duxiu founded Anhui Vernacular Newspaper at the Science Bookstore. They were all in communication. Mr. Zhai's eldest son, Yifu, has a master's degree in political science from the University of Chicago and was once a professor at Nankai University and the head of Jin County. He is currently an inspector at the Jiangsu Construction Department. The second son, Jinfu, has a doctorate in law from Northwestern University and currently works in the Legislative Yuan. Mr. Jinfu's wife, Ms. Cao Meien, also has a master's degree in education from Wittenberg University in the United States. Both are well-known in society.

Apology to Mr. Chen and the Referee Association in Writing

Since the incident in December last year when Chen Jixiang, a member of the Chinese Sports Referees Association, was injured after being beaten while serving as a referee for a Jiangda football match, the sports community in Shanghai has been lamenting and seeing public service as a dangerous path. A Message to the Youth of the Nation 161

Jiang Hengyuan and Yang Weiyu of the China Vocational Education Society, and Liu Zhanen and Pan Wenan of the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute, have discovered that a large number of young people suffer from neurasthenia and recognize this as a great concern for the country. As the former German Chancellor Bismarck said, "If you see how your young people are, you can understand the future of your country." Every time I recite this, I cannot help but sigh deeply. Indeed, the composition of a country must be based on the youth as the main pillars. The rise and fall of a country's destiny depends on whether the youth are excellent or inferior. Is this not the reason? The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute, affiliated with the China Vocational Education Society, has hired health instructors to provide advice to young people who come to the institute. According to reports from the instructors, the most common illness among the young people who come for advice is neurasthenia, accounting for almost nine out of ten. If this is the case in one corner, it can be inferred elsewhere. The colleagues of our society and institute deeply feel that this issue is extremely serious, and dare to express their utmost sincerity to the beloved youth of our country.

A sound mind must reside in a sound body. The mind and body are inherently closely connected. Since the Qin Dynasty, China has emphasized literature over military affairs, which has become a common practice. Scholars despise physical education and do not emphasize vitality. Inherited from their ancestors, their physical condition is already weak. In this era of flourishing science and fierce economic competition, we cannot survive without being enterprising, and we cannot protect ourselves without striving. If we use this physical condition to compete with others, how can we not fail? As a result, our country's production is insufficient, the people's strength is declining, external disasters are urgent, and morale is declining, all of which have been clearly revealed. There are many reasons for this, but poor physical health is one of the main ones. Now, according to reports from the instructors, it has been discovered that the young people who are the main pillars of the country are in such an unfortunate condition. It is truly chilling. We cannot help but recognize that this is a great concern for the country. If we can take measures to save the situation as soon as possible, how can we not hope for the future of our nation?

I have often considered that the causes of neurasthenia are either due to excessive use of the brain, or due to improper sexual impulses and unrestrained indulgence. The former is related to school education, and the latter is related to the social environment, and the latter is even more important than the former. With the development of material civilization and the changes in male-female interaction, the trends are very different from the past. Young people's fragile minds are stimulated, and they chase after them arbitrarily, unable to stop themselves. As a result, they can only sink deeper and deeper. It must be known that desires have no limit to satisfaction, and indulgence is the medium of sin. The temptations of social demons are endless, and the shaking of individual hearts is also irresistible. Distress, depression, pessimism, and world-weariness arise one after another, which is inevitable. To study science diligently, work hard, serve society, and protect the country are all the great expectations that the people of the country have for today's youth, but the youth are already in such a state. Is there anything more heartbreaking in the world?

We colleagues, regarding the authorities of secondary schools, earnestly hope that they can pay close attention to the students' physical and mental health when implementing education. For leaders who bear the responsibility of maintaining morality in society, we earnestly hope that they can be cautious and not set bad examples for future generations. As for the young people who are currently in high school, university, or have graduated from high school or university, their blood and energy are about to be determined, and their knowledge is gradually increasing. We cannot help but have ten thousand wishes, hoping that they can achieve self-reliance through self-reflection.

The desire to improve is inherent in everyone. Material desires should be despised by young people. However, due to the temptation of the environment and the lack of advice, they unconsciously seek temporary pleasure and forget their ambitions. Young people, the boundary between humans and animals and the key to life and death, how can you not distinguish it? At this time, you should carefully compare the advantages and disadvantages and strengthen your determination, so as not to be affected by external things or shaken by external forces, so as to understand your own responsibilities. Have I not completed my studies, mastered my skills, established my character, or erased my shame? Can I be considered a human being? I say no. If not, what should I do? If my clothes are not as good as others, I can still avoid the cold. If my food is not as good as others, I can still avoid hunger. Am I still dissatisfied? Please look at those who are cold and have no clothes, those who are hungry and have no food. What will I do? Protect my body for the service of the country, and protect my country to fulfill my responsibilities. Since I have read books, I should understand this principle. If I do not know how to protect myself or my country, what is the use of reading books? All these things, I sincerely hope that my beloved youth will constantly reflect on themselves in order to achieve self-reliance. The country's heavy responsibility of ten thousand jun (a unit of weight) and the nation's long journey of ten thousand li (a unit of distance) all hope that you will carry it on your shoulders and walk it on your feet.

Do not be trapped by material things, do not indulge in sexual desires, protect your useful body, and diligently engage in reasonable exercise. This is truly the most important responsibility for young people to themselves and to the country. We colleagues truly cannot bear to blame the youth any further, but only sincerely and passionately ask our beloved youth to accept it.

Hengyuan still remembers last year when my friend Mr. Yang returned from Europe and told me what he had seen. One day, he visited a middle school at a German military base and saw fifty or sixty students practicing martial arts naked, with heat evaporating from their faces and backs. At that time, it was the dead of winter, and fine snow was falling in the sky. The visitors were wearing leather coats and still felt cold. After their class was over, they went forward and asked, "Are you not suffering?" Three of the students replied with emotion, "Sir, do you know that Germany has been disarmed? We have no guns to fight the enemy, so we can only forge our bodies into steel to fight them!" When I heard these words, I felt my nerves tremble. Alas, this is what is meant by German youth! How will the future of the German nation be? It can probably be seen from this. Beloved youth of our country, what will your thoughts be after seeing this?

The country is about to fall, and the time will not come again. Words have limits, but intentions are endless. May all the beloved youth of our country take heed of this.

Interviews with Lin and Qiu 166

Lin Baohua: Badminton is one of the most common competitions in the West and is even more popular in England. Overseas Chinese all practice it. Its fun may surpass tennis. One game of badminton is better than one set of tennis. However, in Shanghai, although it has become a common sport among Westerners, the Chinese are indifferent to it. Mr. Qiu's participation this time is intended to promote it. Since there is no venue for this kind of competition, there is no practice. I hope that the Chinese can be interested during the competition.

Qiu Feihai: Very few Chinese in Shanghai play badminton. In Hainan, such as Singapore, many people love it. This competition is indoors, so it is a very good sport for tennis players to practice their skills in winter. It is suitable for both men and women and is full of interest. I hope that the Chinese will start practicing it, organize clubs, prepare venues, compete with foreigners, and win the championship.

Competition Group Formation

The competition is sponsored by the Bu Hai Badminton Club. There are a total of five championships: men's singles, men's doubles, women's doubles, women's singles, and mixed doubles. Ten people participate in the men's singles, eleven groups in the doubles, six people in the women's singles, eight groups in the women's doubles, and eleven groups in the mixed doubles. Since there are no Chinese participants in the women's singles, doubles, and mixed doubles, they are omitted. In the men's competition, Meiyeshi is hopeful for the singles championship. Mei was the champion in 1931. Last year, it was not held due to the Shanghai war. The doubles is also the strongest group with Meiyeshi and Beilunzi. Lin Baohua has the hope of reaching the semifinals against Beilunzi, but in the doubles, they will immediately face the veteran generals Xina and Xue Erfu, and I am afraid they must work hard to cope.

Shanghai College Defeats Zhenru 169

Shanghai College Takes the Lead Right from the Start. Shanghai College used a feint to attack Zhenru directly. Two point guards, Sun Maiqing and Lu Hui, scored five points. Qian Jing罰 scored one point. Zhenru hurriedly defended, losing six points in a row, and then rushed to catch up. Huang Zhaolin used his sharpshooting skills to throw the basketball, catching up with five points.

Zhenru Gradually Reveals Its Edge. Qian Jing罰 added two points for Shanghai College, and Feng Nianhua罰 scored one point, leading 9 to 5. Zhenru did not show weakness, with a well-organized lineup, not flustered at all, pouncing in like a hungry tiger, brave and extraordinary. Huang Zhaolin and Wang Nanzhen scored successively, tying the score at 9 to 9. Shanghai College's Sun and Feng each罚 scored one point, thus taking the lead again by two points. Zhenru's spirit was extraordinary, unstoppable. Old Huang Zhong (Huang Zhaolin) and Yin Guiren scored two goals in a row, surpassing Shanghai College 13 to 11. Shanghai College's Passing Is Excellent. Shanghai College called a timeout, reorganized its forces, and Feng Nianhua scored two long shots, greatly boosting morale, thus surpassing Zhenru again 15 to 13. Han Zhenyuan made it 15-15. Shanghai College's five tigers worked together in perfect harmony, showing excellent short passing, which was magical and breathtaking. The five tigers worked hard, each showing their unique skills. Although Zhenru was strong, they were troubled by the tight defense of each player, with few chances to shoot the basket. Therefore, at the end of the first half, Shanghai College won 27 to 16.

Smooth Sailing From Then On. After the break, Huang Zhaolin of Zhenru罰 scored first, and Xu Rongshui and Han Zhenyuan each scored one, adding five points. Shanghai College, with its tight defense and fierce forwards, had smooth sailing from then on, always victorious. Zhenru, at this point, felt inferior. Although they were still unwilling to show weakness, Huang Zhaolin repeatedly made wonderful long shots, winning praise from the audience. However, the gains did not offset the losses, and it was difficult to recover. The largest score difference was 39 to 23. As a result, Shanghai College won 49 to 37.

Spring and Autumn

Six-Character Couplet 176

— Zhan Lu

I have an old friend, Mr. Ziyang, who has been in politics for a long time and has just returned from Peiping. When we met, after shaking hands and exchanging pleasantries, I asked him about the current political situation. He stroked his goatee and replied, "Where to begin with a history of twenty-four dynasties? But to say a few summarizing words, I once composed a six-character couplet that is not only well-matched but also worth a new exposé of the officialdom." I asked, "What is the six-character couplet?" He said: "Flatter superiors, pass the days; brag loudly, steal the show."

The matching of the six-character couplet is ingenious, truly "the essence of writing is natural, the marvel comes by chance"; but to say that it is worth a new exposé of the officialdom, this scope is too narrow! It must be known that "flatter superiors, pass the days; brag loudly, steal the show" is the meaning of the six-character couplet from any society, ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign; the only difference is the thickness and thinness of the quality!

The power of flattery can encompass everything in the world and more; only because the wheel of time is constantly advancing, everything that cannot keep up will have its day of obsolescence. Sages will become obsolete, classics will become obsolete, science and art will become obsolete; only the flattery experts who are suitable for the past, the present, and the future will never become obsolete! As the saying goes: "A thousand wears, ten thousand wears, flattery never wears out;" this is the ironclad proof that flatterers will not become obsolete.

The habit of bragging cannot be broken by anyone; especially writers, look at the authors of the past and present, who does not do some bragging poetry and prose? Especially merchants, look at the merchants selling around the world, who does not do some bragging commercial advertising? Especially the publicity personnel in the military and political circles, whose bragging is strong, is whose limelight is healthy; their work, besides "bragging loudly, stealing the show", is best described as "not for other use".

Mr. Ziyang's six-character couplet is indeed an unbreakable saying from ancient times to the present, from China to abroad.

Good Things All Turn Bad 177

— Lily

丨Aggressors Should Be Careful of Turning Bad丨

Free love could have overthrown blind marriages. Free love could have been the main road for legitimate unions of men and women. However, in recent years, Chinese young men and women have been talking about free love and marriage freedom, and in the end, nine out of ten, before they even reach formal union, have already loved someone else. "Free love" has become a synonym for illicit cohabitation between men and women.

Opium, morphine, sleeping pills, etc., have always been used for medical purposes in Europe and the United States, and countless patients have benefited from these drugs. But when opium arrived in China, everyone swallowed clouds and spat fog to smoke it, and morphine, etc., were made into red pills and white pills. Sleeping pills have become a direct tool for suicide.

Students go abroad to study. Those who study political science come back to China to specialize in making money and arguing. Those who study military science come back to China to devote themselves to civil war. Is this what these students learned abroad?

Socialism in Soviet Russia has created the amazing achievement of completing the Five-Year Plan in four years, with orderly domestic order and the respect of all countries. But I remember when the Kuomintang and the Communist Party were not divided, socialism was also popular for a while, but the result was that wives killed their husbands, sons killed their fathers, finances went bankrupt, and all industries stagnated, forming a situation of public wives and common property, destroying everything beyond recognition. Even with the recent Communist bandits in Jiangxi, their achievements are nothing more than killing and arson.

The Japanese say: "No matter what it is, if it is good in other countries, it all turns bad when it comes to China." This sentence seems to be somewhat insulting. But when we think carefully, there is some truth in this statement. The examples mentioned above are just a few that have been picked up casually, and they are enough to prove what the Japanese said.

"Oranges change to trifoliate oranges when they cross the Huai River." No matter what it is, it will turn bad when it comes to China, so if someone comes to invade China, we will let them invade. If they do anything on Chinese land, they are guaranteed to fail and end badly.

Hankou Miscellany 178

— Shao Zhenzhi

丨New Year's Eve丨

All industries are competing, and the glass windows are displaying all kinds of goods, all trying to attract customers; and at the door of each house, on average, there is a beggar standing. Especially at night, squatting in front of the streets, yelling on the roads, are they refugees or beggars? They can even surpass the six thousand streetcars and countless well-fed people. This is the impression before January 25.

The snow is fluttering, the hotels are warm, the cinemas are full, the Taoist temples, temples, and Buddhist associations are all ringing bells to pray! The charity halls are, as usual, distributing rice tickets to those who are not really poor and in pain, and the lower-class prostitutes are still selling cold on the streets when people call out in the middle of the night. The cold north wind is constantly bullying them.

Are they not as good as dogs? This is not necessarily the case. In my opinion, people are still smarter.

Let's look at the matter of dogs biting people: when they bite, they bare their teeth and claws and pounce forward regardless of their lives! They don't care if the person being bitten is empty-handed or holding a stick, or even aiming a knife or gun at them! But people, do you think they are so stupid? Usually, when they put on their "two and a half feet" of armed uniform, look how smug they are! But as soon as someone says they are coming to fight, they run faster than dogs! Because they are smarter than dogs, they know: endure humiliation and bear heavy burdens! Don't suffer immediate losses. This is one.

When a dog fails to bite someone, it only "howls" once, tucks its tail, and runs away in a puff of smoke. There is no other action. As for people, that is not the case; the enemy has not yet attacked, and as soon as they put up a fight, they run away without their lives! Their hearts are full of "greed for life and fear of death, and living in ease and comfort"! But they shout out loud: "You all have to calm down, let me slowly call for countermeasures"! May I ask: Is a dog this smart? This is two.

When a dog is beaten, it remembers the hatred: whenever it encounters its enemy, it always bares its teeth and claws! To let its enemy know: I have a deep hatred that has not been avenged! But people, they don't care: even if they break my door, enter my room, and beat me black and blue, as soon as they turn around, they can "drink wine and make peace"! Dogs cannot compare to this kind of magnanimity! This is three.

Also, dogs cannot resist, they tuck their tails and squat.

Novel Photography Ink Escape 179

There was an enemy who could speak Chinese, shouting loudly: "Hey, now the emperor sees that you are very pitiful, and told us to bring a lot of silver dollars to reward you... How can you not understand the rules? Kneel down quickly... Have you all knelt down?... Good, kneel like this, don't move, let us take a photo of you first for the emperor to see, so that he knows that you have all received the reward... Kneel well, don't move, you will receive the reward after the photo is taken..."

More than three thousand men, women, old and young people knelt on the ground with their waists straight and necks straight, staring blankly at the enemy, not knowing what kind of trick he was going to play.

"This won't do, you all have to lower your heads, you can't raise them... Otherwise, if the photo is taken, the emperor will say that you are not respectful, and he won't reward you next time..."

More than three thousand men, women, old and young people listened obediently, and one by one they lowered their heads, looking at the ground. From a distance, it looked like a dark mass of heads hiding in their wings, sleeping birds. As soon as their heads were lowered, their necks were exposed; the snow fell on their skin in clumps, and they could only shake their heads, not daring to use their sleeves to cover them, and had to clench their teeth, rolling their eyelids upwards to peek at how the enemies were taking pictures of them, hoping in their hearts that they would hurry up and take a picture casually. The people kneeling in the first row saw in the corner of their eyes that the enemies were busy setting up tripods, and then installed a dark, shiny cylinder on the tripod. They also saw Japanese soldiers stuffing a cloth strip inside. There were at least seventeen or eight of them surrounding them in a large circle. They were all curious, thinking: Is this cylinder the camera? Are all these people photographed on that cloth strip? They are really lucky today: they can get a reward and open their eyes! Photography...

The people in the middle rows, because their necks were constantly being drenched, and the water turned into ice, which was very uncomfortable, peeked out and saw that several enemies were squatting on the ground, not paying attention to them; they slightly raised their heads to move their necks. (Six)

"Please, Stove God!" "Winter plum, winter plum," "Charcoal, charcoal," "Golden flower, Yuanbin flower," "Large version of the almanac, small version of the almanac," ... Ding ding da da; large baskets and small baskets of "New Year's goods" are very lively.

Firecrackers are louder than machine guns, and the sound of "Congratulations on getting rich" is still as good as in previous years. The phenomenon of "unease" was in Shanghai last year, and this year it is in Peiping. Hankou doesn't need to worry anyway, and just goes on "doing its own thing." Only on January 28 did entertainment stop for one day, and on January 28, a tragedy of "Song Ruhai being hit hard" was staged at the Zhongshan Park ball field.

"Alive, alive," vendors of lantern sell lanterns again.

There are especially many people at Guiyuan Temple in Hanyang, with many red men and green women squeezing in to worship. It is fun and beautiful. "Shang Jiu Wan" and "Yuanxiao" are especially crowded, and other Zen forests cannot compare.

Bronze drums, foreign horns, machine plays, sound machines, and silk strings and gongs and drums, ... modern men and women, fashionable lanterns, beggars, refugees, ... these can be seen and heard in hotels, cinemas, shops, streets and alleys.

However, the content of Hankou is still difficult to figure out?

Are People Not As Good As Dogs? 180

— Fei Fei

丨People Are Still Smarter丨

After reading Mr. Yiyi's great work "Are People Not As Good As Dogs" the other day, it was really flavorful! But after thinking carefully: When a dog is talked about, it bows its head and has nothing to say. However, this is not the case with people. They do not allow you to laugh, do not allow you to cry, and do not allow you to shout! Otherwise, he snorts and immediately tells you to "stop breathing"! How many chapters and articles, how many 'damn'! May I ask: Does a dog have this kind of power? This is four.

The kind of person I mentioned, although not many in our group, really exists! For years, I have been obliged to praise Yang Yizhang's "hidden virtue" and "hidden light"! Its merit is probably no less than Yu's!

Small Knowledge 181

A Short History of Stamps

The stamps used in the world are of many kinds and are constantly emerging, which can be described as the ultimate in variety. Looking at its history, it is ninety-eight years old. The era of the first stamp invention was in 1834. The inventor of the stamp was an Englishman named GuuegGkulmers.

In 1840, the British government had a proposal to create a one-penny stamp, printed on the envelope, and instructed the people to use this kind of stamped envelope. However, because it was not easy to use, the public opposed it, and as a result, they adopted the adhesive stamp invented by Postalers.

The United States did not use stamps until 1847: it also used adhesive stamps. This is a small piece of the history of stamps.

How Many Dialects Are There in the World?

The dialects in the world, including various local languages, number about three thousand four hundred. These dialects, mostly due to the isolation of the climate and the habits that have been passed down, are forever difficult to change. This huge number of dialects naturally mostly belongs to uncivilized savages. There are more than 900 in Asia, more than 600 in Europe, more than 275 in Africa, and more than 1,600 in the Americas.

The Reason for Pain

No matter which part of our body has a sore or is cut by a knife, we will immediately feel pain. But how does the pain process work, and how do we feel it? It is because there is a nerve center on people's backs; from this center, tiny nerves are spread like spider webs all over the body. If an abnormal state occurs in a certain part of our body, the tiny nerves immediately report to the center, and we feel pain. However, the distribution of nerves is denser in some parts, or closer to the skin, and the sensation in those parts is particularly sensitive. Conversely, the sensation is relatively slow and pure. For example, the nerves in the heel of the foot are not close to the skin surface, so the sensation is the slowest.

When we cut a finger, the blood vessels and tiny nerves on the finger are broken at the same time. The sneaky blood cannot be transported back to the heart from the original tube, so it gushes out from the cut, becoming bleeding. At the same time, the tiny nerves report the discomfort to the brain, and we feel pain. Because the skin at the cut is broken and the inside comes into contact with oxygen in the air, the tiny nerves are agitated, and the brain increases the sensation of pain. Therefore, to put it simply, the reason for pain is just a feeling caused by nerve agitation. For example, when cutting a disease in a hospital, the nerves in the area to be cut are anesthetized first, and the patient will not feel pain when cutting; also, if the dentist removes the nerves of a decayed tooth using anesthesia, although the decayed tooth still exists, the patient will never experience pain again. That is because the nerves have lost the ability to report, and the brain is like a person in Peach Blossom Spring who does not hear about outside affairs, and will forever live in a numb and peaceful world, without feeling pain!

How Do We Feel Hungry?

Hunger, jokingly speaking, is "the stomach is doing mischief," but a further understanding is that the stomach needs food. But according to physiology, the second theory is also seemingly right. Because human blood is constantly circulating and growing, and when the time is right, the materials for making new blood are declared to be lacking; this report of lacking blood materials reaches the stomach, and people feel hungry. Because people's food, when it reaches the stomach, absorbs the essential elements from the food through the stomach and mixes it with another kind of juice to make new blood. Therefore, the stomach is just a factory for making blood. It can be seen that the reason for human hunger is not just a matter of the stomach, but the whole body needs new blood materials. We can use extremely simple facts to prove this. A person who is extremely hungry only needs to inject the materials for making blood into the large intestine, and even if it does not pass through the stomach, the person's hunger can be alleviated and eaten.

Financial News: Gold Price Rises, Buyers Delighted 182

Yesterday, foreign dispatches indicated: London spot and forward rates both rose 0.0625; the British-American exchange rate hesitantly rose 3.75; the American-British exchange rate rose 1.875; the New York silver price appeared to rise 0.25, but in reality, the increase was not significant, as it remained unchanged from last Saturday; forward silver prices only rose 0.003 to 0.009, which was also insignificant; a bank private dispatch showed a rise of 0.0625; American cotton fell 0.05-0.06 pounds. Therefore, although the Shanghai gold market opened low, it remained relatively stable, at 787.2 taels. The exchange market saw April U.S. dollars hard to sell at 28.625 yuan, dropping to 5.8 taels. Afterwards, prices trended higher, with major players actively buying, including Heng Yu, Fu Yu, and Yuan Mao competing to purchase large quantities. The exchange market also tightened. The Yokohama Specie Bank frequently engaged in arbitrage, buying up current-month U.S. dollars at 3.75, pushing through the 90 tael barrier, and further arbitraging the same month at 3.125, reaching 793.4 taels. The midday close was at 3.1 taels. In the afternoon, prices initially rose and then stabilized. Zhejiang bought up April U.S. dollars at 3.75, further fueled by May already trading at 5.625, pushing the price to 94.3 taels. Both the exchange and gold markets then gradually turned back. Banque Belge bought February U.S. dollars at 3.125, and Hefeng offered March at 3.75, leading to a downward trend. Furthermore, American Express sold March at 4.375, causing a drop to 1.8 taels. Major players forcefully supported the market, pulling prices back and hovering around 2 taels. Finally, the market closed at 792.3 taels. The sentiment throughout the day was extremely positive, with major players all buying in, demand exceeding supply, justifying the price increase. The Central Bank’s spot market was weaker and extremely quiet today. Swap spreads were still posted by short sellers, with slightly higher prices, ranging from 1.2 to 1.3 taels, but trading volume was minimal. The daily market conditions are detailed below:

Breaking 90 Taels 183

Soon after, the market closed at 793.1 taels. Arbitrageurs sold at 2.8 taels.

Gradual Stabilization After Rise 184

The afternoon opened at 792.8 taels. Initially, the market was extremely quiet, hovering around 3 taels for a long time. Before long, Hengyu buying in boosted the market, reaching 4 taels. Zhifeng Yong, limited by its trading limit, sold at 4 taels, temporarily halting the advance and retreating to 3.5 taels. Richang and Yuanmao Yong bought in, but Fuchang and Hengxing sold, resulting in weak trading activity, taking a long time. Later, Zhejiang buying up April U.S. dollars at 3.75 pushed the market beyond 4 taels to 94.3 taels. Dadecheng made slight advances around 4 taels. Although retail investors sold, the market was still able to hold. When East Asia sold May U.S. dollars at 5.625, the market retreated within 4 taels. Reversal of Fortune for Jiao Coins 194

In late January of this year, which was the Lunar New Year holiday, due to the customary practice of small money shops, there was a significant surge in auxiliary currency at the end of the year. Therefore, many small money shops hoarded large quantities of Dalian double jiao coins in their warehouses, and mortgaged them to banks and money shops, hoping to get a good price at the time and seek a hefty profit. Unexpectedly, this time during the New Year holiday, a large batch of spot jiao coins from Dalian was shipped to Shanghai, and the areas along the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and the Yangtze River, knowing that jiao coins would rise at the end of the year, all shipped large quantities to Shanghai without prior agreement. Unexpectedly, the goods became stagnant upon arrival, overwhelming the market. In recent days, spot goods have been abundant. The large quantities of spot goods hoarded by Shanghai money shops were mortgaged and had to be sold off when the mortgages expired. As a result, they sold off their goods one after another, and market prices fell sharply. Yesterday, the exchange rate was so bad that it was possible to exchange 12.01 jiao for one yuan. This was truly an unexpected and special market situation.
